href="#cite_note-GVA-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><span style="font-weight:normal;">&#160;\xe2\x80\xa2 Per capita</span></th><td>\n\xc2\xa326,159 ($37,747, PPP<sup id="cite_ref-imf.org_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imf.org-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>)<sup id="cite_ref-GVA_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GVA-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">\n</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Currency</th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">Pound&#160;sterling</a> (<a href="/wiki/ISO_4217" title="ISO 4217">GBP</a>;&#160;<a href="/wiki/Pound_sign" title="Pound sign">\xc2\xa3</a>)</td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row">Time zone</th><td>\n<span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">UTC</a>&#8288;</span> (<a href="/wiki/Greenwich_Mean_Time" title="Greenwich Mean Time">Greenwich Mean Time</a>)</td></tr><tr class="mergedbottomrow"><th scope="row"><div style="text-indent:-0.9em;margin-left:1.2em;font-weight:normal;">\xe2\x80\xa2&#160;Summer&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Daylight_saving_time" title="Daylight saving time">DST</a>)</div></th><td>\n<span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">UTC</a>+1</span> (<a href="/wiki/British_Summer_Time" title="British Summer Time">British Summer Time</a>)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Date format</th><td>\ndd/mm/yyyy&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Anno_Domini" title="Anno Domini">AD</a>)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Left-_and_right-hand_traffic" title="Left- and right-hand traffic">Driving side</a></th><td>\nleft</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Telephone_numbers_in_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Telephone numbers in England">Calling code</a></th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/Telephone_numbers_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Telephone numbers in the United Kingdom">+44</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Patron_saint" title="Patron saint">Patron saint</a></th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/Saint_George" title="Saint George">Saint George</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/ISO_3166" title="ISO 3166">ISO 3166 code</a></th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/ISO_3166-2:GB-ENG" class="mw-redirect" title="ISO 3166-2:GB-ENG">GB-ENG</a></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="text-align:left;margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;"><ol style="list-style-type: lower-alpha; margin-left: 1em; font-size:90%;">\n<li value="1"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_footnote_a"><b><a href="#ref_footnote_a">^</a></b></span>  While England does not have its own legislative assembly, a <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Grand_Committee" title="Legislative Grand Committee">Legislative Grand Committee</a> composed of only the 533 MPs representing English constituencies can scrutinise and vote on bills going through parliament which only affect England.</li>\n</ol></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>England</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Country" title="Country">country</a> that is <a href="/wiki/Countries_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Countries of the United Kingdom">part</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> It shares land borders with <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> to the north and <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a> to the west. The <a href="/wiki/Irish_Sea" title="Irish Sea">Irish Sea</a> lies northwest of England and the <a href="/wiki/Celtic_Sea" title="Celtic Sea">Celtic Sea</a> lies to the southwest. England is separated from <a href="/wiki/Continental_Europe" title="Continental Europe">continental Europe</a> by the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a> to the east and the <a href="/wiki/English_Channel" title="English Channel">English Channel</a> to the south. The country covers five-eighths of the island of <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a>, which lies in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean#Northern_Atlantic" title="Atlantic Ocean">North Atlantic</a>, and includes <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_England" title="List of islands of England">over 100 smaller islands</a>, such as the <a href="/wiki/Isles_of_Scilly" title="Isles of Scilly">Isles of Scilly</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Wight" title="Isle of Wight">Isle of Wight</a>.\n</p><p>The area now called England was first inhabited by modern humans during the <a href="/wiki/Upper_Palaeolithic" class="mw-redirect" title="Upper Palaeolithic">Upper Palaeolithic</a> period, but takes its name from the <a href="/wiki/Angles" title="Angles">Angles</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic</a> tribe deriving its name from the <a href="/wiki/Anglia_(peninsula)" title="Anglia (peninsula)">Anglia</a> peninsula, who settled during the 5th and 6th centuries. England became a unified state in the 10th century, and since the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">Age of Discovery</a>, which began during the 15th century, has had a significant cultural and legal impact on the wider world.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The English language, the <a href="/wiki/Anglican_Communion" title="Anglican Communion">Anglican Church</a>, and <a href="/wiki/English_law" title="English law">English law</a> \xe2\x80\x93 the basis for the <a href="/wiki/Common_law" title="Common law">common law</a> legal systems of many other countries around the world \xe2\x80\x93 developed in England, and the country\'s <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">parliamentary system</a> of government has been widely adopted by other nations.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a> began in 18th-century England, transforming its society into the world\'s first industrialised nation.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>England\'s terrain is chiefly low hills and <a href="/wiki/Plain" title="Plain">plains</a>, especially in central and southern England. However, there is upland and mountainous terrain in the north (for example, the <a href="/wiki/Lake_District" title="Lake District">Lake District</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pennines" title="Pennines">Pennines</a>) and in the west (for example, <a href="/wiki/Dartmoor" title="Dartmoor">Dartmoor</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Shropshire_Hills" title="Shropshire Hills">Shropshire Hills</a>). The capital is London, which has the largest metropolitan area in both the United Kingdom and the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;nb 1&#93;</a></sup> England\'s population of over 55&#160;million comprises 84% of the population of the United Kingdom,<sup id="cite_ref-ONS-pop-ests-June2018_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ONS-pop-ests-June2018-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> largely concentrated around London, the <a href="/wiki/South_East_England" title="South East England">South East</a>, and conurbations in the <a href="/wiki/English_Midlands" class="mw-redirect" title="English Midlands">Midlands</a>, the <a href="/wiki/North_West_England" title="North West England">North West</a>, the <a href="/wiki/North_East_England" title="North East England">North East</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire" title="Yorkshire">Yorkshire</a>, which each developed as major industrial regions during the 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-2011census_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011census-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">Kingdom of England</a> \xe2\x80\x93 which after 1535 included Wales \xe2\x80\x93 ceased being a separate <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> on 1 May 1707, when the <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Union_1707" title="Acts of Union 1707">Acts of Union</a> put into effect the terms agreed in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Union" title="Treaty of Union">Treaty of Union</a> the previous year, resulting in a political union with the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Scotland" title="Kingdom of Scotland">Kingdom of Scotland</a> to create the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Kingdom of Great Britain</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> In 1801, Great Britain was united with the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Ireland" title="Kingdom of Ireland">Kingdom of Ireland</a> (through another <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Union,_1800" class="mw-redirect" title="Acts of Union, 1800">Act of Union</a>) to become the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland</a>. In 1922 the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Free_State" title="Irish Free State">Irish Free State</a> seceded from the United Kingdom, leading to the latter being <a href="/wiki/Royal_and_Parliamentary_Titles_Act_1927" title="Royal and Parliamentary Titles Act 1927">renamed</a> the United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toclevel-2 tocsection-28"><a href="#Visual_arts"><span class="tocnumber">9.4</span> <span class="toctext">Visual arts</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-29"><a href="#Literature,_poetry,_and_philosophy"><span class="tocnumber">9.5</span> <span class="toctext">Literature, poetry, and philosophy</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-30"><a class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-36"><a href="#Notes"><span
