London</a></div>\n<div style="position:absolute; text-align:right; font-size:85%; left:297.85px; top:95px"><a href="/wiki/Tyne_and_Wear" title="Tyne and Wear">Tyne &amp;<br />Wear</a></div>\n       <div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:205.15px; top:136.2px"><a href="/wiki/Cumbria" title="Cumbria">Cumbria</a></div>\n       <div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:282.4px; top:172.25px"><a href="/wiki/North_Yorkshire" title="North Yorkshire">North Yorkshire</a></div>\n       <div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:303px; top:244.35px"><a href="/wiki/South_Yorkshire" title="South Yorkshire">South<br />Yorks.</a></div>\n       <div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:277.25px; top:213.45px"><a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire" title="West Yorkshire">West<br />Yorkshire</a></div>\n       <div style="position:absolute; text-align:right; font-size:85%; left:244.805px; top:239.2px"><a href="/wiki/Greater_Manchester" title="Greater Manchester">Greater<br />Manc.</a></div>\n       <div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:187.125px; top:249.5px"><a href="/wiki/Merseyside" title="Merseyside">Merseyside</a></div>\n       <div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:395.7px; top:494.125px"><a href="/wiki/East_Sussex" title="East Sussex">East<br />Sussex</a></div>\n       <div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:349.35px; top:494.125px"><a href="/wiki/West_Sussex" title="West Sussex">West<br />Sussex</a></div>\n       <div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:305.575px; top:532.75px"><a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Wight" title="Isle of Wight"> Isle of<br />Wight</a></div>\n       <div style="position:absolute; text-align:left; font-size:85%; left:272.1px; top:342.2px"><a href="/wiki/West_Midlands_(county)" title="West Midlands (county)">West<br />Midlands</a></div>\n</div></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Ceremonial_counties_of_England" title="Ceremonial counties of England">Ceremonial counties of England</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Subdivisions_of_England" title="Subdivisions of England">subdivisions of England</a> consist of up to four levels of <a href="/wiki/Administrative_division" title="Administrative division">subnational division</a> controlled through a variety of types of administrative entities created for the purposes of <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_England" title="Local government in England">local government</a>. The highest tier of local government were the nine <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_England" title="Regions of England">regions of England</a>: <a href="/wiki/North_East_England" title="North East England">North East</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_West_England" title="North West England">North West</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_and_the_Humber" title="Yorkshire and the Humber">Yorkshire and the Humber</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands" title="East Midlands">East Midlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Midlands_(region)" title="West Midlands (region)">West Midlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_of_England" title="East of England">East</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_East_England" title="South East England">South East</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_West_England" title="South West England">South West</a>, and London. These were created in 1994 as <a href="/wiki/Government_Office" title="Government Office">Government Offices</a>, used by the UK government to deliver a wide range of policies and programmes regionally, but there are no elected bodies at this level, except in London, and in 2011 the regional government offices were abolished.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> The same boundaries remain in use for electing <a href="/wiki/Members_of_the_European_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Members of the European Parliament">Members of the European Parliament</a> on a regional basis.\n</p><p>After <a href="/wiki/Devolution" title="Devolution">devolution</a> began to take place in other parts of the United Kingdom it was planned that referendums for the regions of England would take place for their own elected <a href="/wiki/Regional_Assemblies_in_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Regional Assemblies in England">regional assemblies</a> as a counterweight. <a href="/wiki/Greater_London_Authority_referendum,_1998" title="Greater London Authority referendum, 1998">London accepted</a> in 1998: the <a href="/wiki/London_Assembly" title="London Assembly">London Assembly</a> was created two years later. However, when the proposal was rejected by the <a href="/wiki/Northern_England_devolution_referendums,_2004" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern England devolution referendums, 2004">northern England devolution referendums, 2004</a> in the North East, further referendums were cancelled.<sup id="cite_ref-refreject_95-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-refreject-95">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> The regional assemblies outside London were abolished in 2010, and their functions transferred to respective <a href="/wiki/Regional_Development_Agency" class="mw-redirect" title="Regional Development Agency">Regional Development Agencies</a> and a new system of <a href="/wiki/Local_authority_leaders%27_boards" class="mw-redirect" title="Local authority leaders&#39; boards">Local authority leaders\' boards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Below the regional level, all of England is divided into 48 <a href="/wiki/Ceremonial_counties_of_England" title="Ceremonial counties of England">ceremonial counties</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-britannicagov_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannicagov-115">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> These are used primarily as a geographical frame of reference and have developed gradually since the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, with some established as recently as 1974.<sup id="cite_ref-maud_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-maud-116">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Each has a <a href="/wiki/Lord_Lieutenant" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Lieutenant">Lord Lieutenant</a> and <a href="/wiki/High_Sheriff" class="mw-redirect" title="High Sheriff">High Sheriff</a>; these posts are used to represent the <a href="/wiki/British_monarch" class="mw-redirect" title="British monarch">British monarch</a> locally.<sup id="cite_ref-britannicagov_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannicagov-115">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> Outside <a href="/wiki/Greater_London" title="Greater London">Greater London</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Isles_of_Scilly" title="Isles of Scilly">Isles of Scilly</a>, England is also divided into 83 <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_and_non-metropolitan_counties_of_England" title="Metropolitan and non-metropolitan counties of England">metropolitan and non-metropolitan counties</a>; these correspond to areas used for the purposes of local government<sup id="cite_ref-localgov_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-localgov-117">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> and may consist of a single district or be divided into several.\n</p><p>There are six <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_county" title="Metropolitan county">metropolitan counties</a> based on the most heavily urbanised areas, which do not have county councils.<sup id="cite_ref-localgov_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-localgov-117">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> In these areas the principal authorities are the councils of the subdivisions, the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_borough" title="Metropolitan borough">metropolitan boroughs</a>. Elsewhere, 27 <a href="/wiki/Non-metropolitan_county" title="Non-metropolitan county">non-metropolitan "shire" counties</a> have a <a href="/wiki/County_council" title="County council">county council</a> and are divided into districts, each with a district council. They are typically, though not always, found in more rural areas. The remaining non-metropolitan counties are of a single district and usually correspond to large towns or sparsely populated counties; they are known as <a href="/wiki/Unitary_authorities_of_England" title="Unitary authorities of England">unitary authorities</a>. Greater London has a different system for local government, with 32 <a href="/wiki/London_borough" class="mw-redirect" title="London borough">London boroughs</a>, plus the <a href="/wiki/City_of_London" title="City of London">City of London</a> covering a small area at the core governed by the <a href="/wiki/City_of_London_Corporation" title="City of London Corporation">City of London Corporation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> At the most localised level, much of England is divided into <a href="/wiki/Civil_parishes_in_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Civil parishes in England">civil parishes</a> with <a href="/wiki/Parish_councils_in_England" title="Parish councils in England">councils</a>; in Greater London only one, <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Park,_London" title="Queen&#39;s Park, London">Queen\'s Park</a>, exists <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Park,_London#Governance" title="Queen&#39;s Park, London">as of 2014</a> after they were <a href="/wiki/London_Government_Act_1963" title="London Government Act 1963">abolished in 1965</a> until legislation <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_and_Public_Involvement_in_Health_Act_2007" title="Local Government and Public Involvement in Health Act 2007">allowed their recreation</a> in 2007.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_England" title="Geography of England">Geography of England</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Landscape_and_rivers">Landscape and rivers</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Keswick_Panorama_-_Oct_2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Blue lake between green hills." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Keswick_Panorama_-_Oct_2009.jpg/330px-Keswick_Panorama_-_Oct_2009.jpg" width="330" height="117" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Keswick_Panorama_-_Oct_2009.jpg/495px-Keswick_Panorama_-_Oct_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Keswick_Panorama_-_Oct_2009.jpg/660px-Keswick_Panorama_-_Oct_2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="10814" data-file-height="3822" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Keswick_Panorama_-_Oct_2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Skiddaw" title="Skiddaw">Skiddaw</a> massif, seen from <a href="/wiki/Walla_Crag" title="Walla Crag">Walla Crag</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Lake_District" title="Lake District">Lake District</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Geographically England includes the central and southern two-thirds of the island of Great Britain, plus such offshore islands as the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Wight" title="Isle of Wight">Isle of Wight</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Isles_of_Scilly" title="Isles of Scilly">Isles of Scilly</a>. It is bordered by two other countries of the United Kingdom: <a href="/wiki/Anglo_Scottish_border" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo Scottish border">to the north</a> by Scotland and <a href="/wiki/Wales-England_border" class="mw-redirect" title="Wales-England border">to the west</a> by Wales. England is closer to the European continent than any other part of mainland Britain. It is separated from <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> (<a href="/wiki/Hauts-de-France" title="Hauts-de-France">Hauts-de-France</a>) by a 21-mile (34&#160;km)<sup id="cite_ref-Engchannel_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Engchannel-119">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> sea gap, though the two countries are connected by the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Tunnel" title="Channel Tunnel">Channel Tunnel</a> near <a href="/wiki/Folkestone" title="Folkestone">Folkestone</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> England also has shores on the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Sea" title="Irish Sea">Irish Sea</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a> and Atlantic Ocean.\n</p><p>The ports of London, <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_upon_Tyne" title="Newcastle upon Tyne">Newcastle</a> lie on the tidal rivers <a href="/wiki/River_Thames" title="River Thames">Thames</a>, <a href="/wiki/River_Mersey" title="River Mersey">Mersey</a> and <a href="/wiki/River_Tyne" title="River Tyne">Tyne</a> respectively. At 220 miles (350&#160;km), the <a href="/wiki/River_Severn" title="River Severn">Severn</a> is the longest river flowing through England.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> It empties into the <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Channel" title="Bristol Channel">Bristol Channel</a> and is notable for its <a href="/wiki/Severn_Bore" class="mw-redirect" title="Severn Bore">Severn Bore</a> (a <a href="/wiki/Tidal_bore" title="Tidal bore">tidal bore</a>), which can reach 2 metres (6.6&#160;ft) in height.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> However, the longest river entirely in England is the Thames, which is 215 miles (346&#160;km) in length.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames-123">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> There are many <a href="/wiki/Lakes_in_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Lakes in England">lakes in England</a>; the largest is <a href="/wiki/Windermere" title="Windermere">Windermere</a>, within the aptly named <a href="/wiki/Lake_District" title="Lake District">Lake District</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-metoffice_nw_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-metoffice_nw-124">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Most of England\'s landscape consists of low hills and plains, with upland and mountainous terrain in the north and west of the country. The northern uplands include the <a href="/wiki/Pennines" title="Pennines">Pennines</a>, a chain of uplands dividing east and west, the Lake District mountains in Cumbria, and the <a href="/wiki/Cheviot_Hills" title="Cheviot Hills">Cheviot Hills</a>, straddling the border between England and Scotland. The highest point in England, at 978 metres (3,209&#160;ft), is <a href="/wiki/Scafell_Pike" title="Scafell Pike">Scafell Pike</a> in the Lake District.<sup id="cite_ref-metoffice_nw_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-metoffice_nw-124">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Shropshire_Hills" title="Shropshire Hills">Shropshire Hills</a> are near Wales while <a href="/wiki/Dartmoor" title="Dartmoor">Dartmoor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Exmoor" title="Exmoor">Exmoor</a> are two upland areas in the south-west of the country. The approximate dividing line between terrain types is often indicated by the <a href="/wiki/Tees-Exe_line" title="Tees-Exe line">Tees-Exe line</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Widecombe_in_the_Moor,_Devon.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Green hills with trees in the foreground." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Widecombe_in_the_Moor%2C_Devon.jpg/220px-Widecombe_in_the_Moor%2C_Devon.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Widecombe_in_the_Moor%2C_Devon.jpg/330px-Widecombe_in_the_Moor%2C_Devon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Widecombe_in_the_Moor%2C_Devon.jpg/440px-Widecombe_in_the_Moor%2C_Devon.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="1277" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Widecombe_in_the_Moor,_Devon.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Terrain of <a href="/wiki/Dartmoor" title="Dartmoor">Dartmoor</a>, Devon</div></div></div>\n<p>In geological terms, the Pennines, known as the "backbone of England", are the oldest range of mountains in the country, originating from the end of the <a href="/wiki/Paleozoic_Era" class="mw-redirect" title="Paleozoic Era">Paleozoic Era</a> around 300&#160;million years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> Their geological composition includes, among others, <a href="/wiki/Sandstone" title="Sandstone">sandstone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a>, and also coal. There are <a href="/wiki/Karst" title="Karst">karst</a> landscapes in calcite areas such as parts of Yorkshire and <a href="/wiki/Derbyshire" title="Derbyshire">Derbyshire</a>. The Pennine landscape is high <a href="/wiki/Moorland" title="Moorland">moorland</a> in upland areas, indented by fertile valleys of the region\'s rivers. They contain two <a href="/wiki/National_parks_in_England" class="mw-redirect" title="National parks in England">national parks</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Dales" title="Yorkshire Dales">Yorkshire Dales</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Peak_District" title="Peak District">Peak District</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/West_Country" title="West Country">West Country</a>, Dartmoor and Exmoor of the Southwest Peninsula include upland moorland supported by granite, and enjoy a <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_south-west_England" title="Climate of south-west England">mild climate</a>; both are national parks.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/English_Lowlands_beech_forests" title="English Lowlands beech forests">English Lowlands</a> are in the central and southern regions of the country, consisting of green rolling hills, including the <a href="/wiki/Cotswold_Hills" class="mw-redirect" title="Cotswold Hills">Cotswold Hills</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chiltern_Hills" title="Chiltern Hills">Chiltern Hills</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Downs" title="North Downs">North</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Downs" title="South Downs">South Downs</a>; where they meet the sea they form white rock exposures such as the <a href="/wiki/Cliffs_of_Dover" class="mw-redirect" title="Cliffs of Dover">cliffs of Dover</a>. This also includes relatively flat plains such as the <a href="/wiki/Salisbury_Plain" title="Salisbury Plain">Salisbury Plain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Somerset_Levels" title="Somerset Levels">Somerset Levels</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Coast_Plain" title="South Coast Plain">South Coast Plain</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Fens" title="The Fens">The Fens</a>.\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate of England">Climate of England</a></div>\n<p>England has a <a href="/wiki/Temperate_climate" title="Temperate climate">temperate</a> <a href="/wiki/Maritime_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Maritime climate">maritime climate</a>: it is mild with temperatures not much lower than 0&#160;\xc2\xb0C (32&#160;\xc2\xb0F) in winter and not much higher than 32&#160;\xc2\xb0C (90&#160;\xc2\xb0F) in summer.<sup id="cite_ref-weather_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-weather-128">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> The weather is damp relatively frequently and is changeable. The coldest months are January and February, the latter particularly on the <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Geography of the United Kingdom">English coast</a>, while July is normally the warmest month. Months with mild to warm weather are May, June, September and October.<sup id="cite_ref-weather_128-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-weather-128">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> Rainfall is spread fairly evenly throughout the year.\n</p><p>Important influences on the climate of England are its proximity to the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>, its northern <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">latitude</a> and the warming of the sea by the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Stream" title="Gulf Stream">Gulf Stream</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-weather_128-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-weather-128">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> Rainfall is higher in the west, and parts of the <a href="/wiki/Lake_District" title="Lake District">Lake District</a> receive more rain than anywhere else in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-weather_128-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-weather-128">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> Since weather records began, the highest temperature recorded was 38.5&#160;\xc2\xb0C (101.3&#160;\xc2\xb0F) on 10 August 2003 at <a href="/wiki/Brogdale" title="Brogdale">Brogdale</a> in Kent,<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> while the lowest was \xe2\x88\x9226.1&#160;\xc2\xb0C (\xe2\x88\x9215.0&#160;\xc2\xb0F) on 10 January 1982 in <a href="/wiki/Edgmond,_Shropshire" title="Edgmond, Shropshire">Edgmond</a>, Shropshire.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Major_conurbations">Major conurbations</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_places_in_England" title="List of places in England">List of places in England</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Greater_London_Built-up_Area" title="Greater London Built-up Area">Greater London Built-up Area</a> is by far the largest urban area in England<sup id="cite_ref-BUA_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BUA-131">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> and one of the busiest cities in the world. It is considered a <a href="/wiki/Global_city" title="Global city">global city</a> and has a population larger than other countries in the United Kingdom besides England itself.<sup id="cite_ref-BUA_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BUA-131">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> Other urban areas of considerable size and influence tend to be in <a href="/wiki/Northern_England" title="Northern England">northern England</a> or the <a href="/wiki/English_Midlands" class="mw-redirect" title="English Midlands">English Midlands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BUA_131-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BUA-131">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> There are <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of cities in the United Kingdom">50 settlements</a> which have been designated <a href="/wiki/City_status_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="City status in the United Kingdom">city status in England</a>, while the wider United Kingdom has 66.\n</p><p>While many cities in England are quite large, such as <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sheffield" title="Sheffield">Sheffield</a>, Manchester, <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a>, <a href="/wiki/City_of_Leeds" title="City of Leeds">Leeds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_upon_Tyne" title="Newcastle upon Tyne">Newcastle</a>, <a href="/wiki/City_of_Bradford" title="City of Bradford">Bradford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nottingham" title="Nottingham">Nottingham</a>, population size is not a prerequisite for city status.<sup id="cite_ref-cathcities_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cathcities-132">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> Traditionally the status was given to towns with <a href="/wiki/List_of_cathedrals_in_England_and_Wales" title="List of cathedrals in England and Wales">diocesan cathedrals</a>, so there are smaller cities like <a href="/wiki/Wells,_Somerset" title="Wells, Somerset">Wells</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ely,_Cambridgeshire" title="Ely, Cambridgeshire">Ely</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ripon" title="Ripon">Ripon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Truro" title="Truro">Truro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chichester" title="Chichester">Chichester</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cathcities_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cathcities-132">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Office_for_National_Statistics" title="Office for National Statistics">Office for National Statistics</a>, the ten largest, continuous built-up urban areas are:<sup id="cite_ref-BUA_131-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BUA-131">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Rank\n</th>\n<th>Urban area\n</th>\n<th>Population\n</th>\n<th width="380pt">Major localities\n</th></tr>\n<tr style="text-align:center;">\n<td>1</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/Greater_London_Built-up_Area" title="Greater London Built-up Area">Greater London Built-up Area</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">9,787,426</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/Greater_London" title="Greater London">Greater London</a>, divided into the <a href="/wiki/City_of_London" title="City of London">City of London</a> and 32 <a href="/wiki/London_borough" class="mw-redirect" title="London borough">London boroughs</a> including <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Croydon" title="London Borough of Croydon">Croydon</a>, <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Barnet" title="London Borough of Barnet">Barnet</a>, <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Ealing" title="London Borough of Ealing">Ealing</a>, <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Bromley" title="London Borough of Bromley">Bromley</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr Area</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">2,553,379</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salford,_Greater_Manchester" Tyne">Newcastle</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Shields" title="North Shields">North Shields</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Shields" title="South Shields">South Shields</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gateshead" Nottinghamshire">Stapleford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlton,_Nottinghamshire" title="Carlton, Nottinghamshire">Carlton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Long_Eaton" title="Long Eaton">Long Eaton</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr href="/wiki/Rawmarsh" title="Rawmarsh">Rawmarsh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Killamarsh" title="Killamarsh">Killamarsh</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="text-align:center;">\n<td>10</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/Bristol_Built-up_Area" title="Bristol Built-up Area">Bristol Built-up Area</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">617,280</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">Bristol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingswood,_South_Gloucestershire" title="Kingswood, South Gloucestershire">Kingswood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mangotsfield" title="Mangotsfield">Mangotsfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stoke_Gifford" title="Stoke Gifford">Stoke Gifford</a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_England" title="Economy of England">Economy of England</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2016-02_City_of_London.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/2016-02_City_of_London.jpg/220px-2016-02_City_of_London.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/2016-02_City_of_London.jpg/330px-2016-02_City_of_London.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/2016-02_City_of_London.jpg/440px-2016-02_City_of_London.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6000" data-file-height="4000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2016-02_City_of_London.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/City_of_London" title="City of London">City of London</a> is the financial capital of United Kingdom<sup id="cite_ref-London_vs._New_York_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-London_vs._New_York-133">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Global_Financial_Centres_Index_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Global_Financial_Centres_Index-134">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>England\'s economy is one of the largest in the world, with an average <a href="/wiki/GDP_per_capita" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP per capita">GDP per capita</a> of \xc2\xa322,907.<sup id="cite_ref-regionalacc_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regionalacc-135">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> Usually regarded as a <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxon_economy" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-Saxon economy">mixed market economy</a>, it has adopted many <a href="/wiki/Free_market" title="Free market">free market</a> principles, yet maintains an advanced social welfare infrastructure.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> The official currency in England is the <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">pound sterling</a>, whose <a href="/wiki/ISO_4217" title="ISO 4217">ISO 4217</a> code is GBP. <a href="/wiki/Taxation_in_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Taxation in England">Taxation in England</a> is quite competitive when <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_tax_rates" title="List of countries by tax rates">compared</a> to much of the rest of Europe \xe2\x80\x93 as of  2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=England&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> the basic rate of personal tax is 20% on taxable income up to \xc2\xa331,865 above the personal tax-free allowance (normally \xc2\xa310,000), and 40% on any additional earnings above that amount.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The economy of England is the largest part of the <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Economy of the United Kingdom">UK\'s economy</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-regionalacc_135-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regionalacc-135">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> which has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita">18th</a> highest GDP <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">PPP</a> per capita in the world. England is a leader in the chemical<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> and pharmaceutical sectors and in key technical industries, particularly <a href="/wiki/Aerospace" title="Aerospace">aerospace</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Arms_industry" title="Arms industry">arms industry</a>, and the manufacturing side of the <a href="/wiki/Software_industry" title="Software industry">software industry</a>. London, home to the <a href="/wiki/London_Stock_Exchange" title="London Stock Exchange">London Stock Exchange</a>, the United Kingdom\'s main <a href="/wiki/Stock_exchange" title="Stock exchange">stock exchange</a> and the largest in Europe, is England\'s financial centre, with 100 of Europe\'s 500&#160;largest corporations being based there.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> London is the largest financial centre in Europe, and as of  2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=England&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> is the second largest in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bentley_Mulsanne_%E2%80%93_Frontansicht_(1),_30._August_2011,_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A grey coloured car." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Bentley_Mulsanne_%E2%80%93_Frontansicht_%281%29%2C_30._August_2011%2C_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg/220px-Bentley_Mulsanne_%E2%80%93_Frontansicht_%281%29%2C_30._August_2011%2C_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg" width="220" height="100" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Bentley_Mulsanne_%E2%80%93_Frontansicht_%281%29%2C_30._August_2011%2C_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg/330px-Bentley_Mulsanne_%E2%80%93_Frontansicht_%281%29%2C_30._August_2011%2C_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Bentley_Mulsanne_%E2%80%93_Frontansicht_%281%29%2C_30._August_2011%2C_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg/440px-Bentley_Mulsanne_%E2%80%93_Frontansicht_%281%29%2C_30._August_2011%2C_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2283" data-file-height="1038" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bentley_Mulsanne_%E2%80%93_Frontansicht_(1),_30._August_2011,_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Bentley_Mulsanne_(2010)" title="Bentley Mulsanne (2010)">Bentley Mulsanne</a>. <a href="/wiki/Bentley" title="Bentley">Bentley</a> is a well-known English car company</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_England" title="Bank of England">Bank of England</a>, founded in 1694 by Scottish banker <a href="/wiki/William_Paterson_(banker)" title="William Paterson (banker)">William Paterson</a>, is the United Kingdom\'s <a href="/wiki/Central_bank" title="Central bank">central bank</a>. Originally established as private banker to the government of England, since 1946 it has been a <a href="/wiki/Nationalisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Nationalisation">state-owned institution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> The bank has a monopoly on the issue of banknotes in <a href="/wiki/England_and_Wales" title="England and Wales">England and Wales</a>, although not in other parts of the United Kingdom. The government has devolved responsibility to the bank\'s <a href="/wiki/Monetary_Policy_Committee" title="Monetary Policy Committee">Monetary Policy Committee</a> for managing the monetary policy of the country and setting interest rates.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>England is highly industrialised, but since the 1970s there has been a decline in traditional heavy and manufacturing industries, and an increasing emphasis on a more <a href="/wiki/Service_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Service industry">service industry</a> oriented economy.<sup id="cite_ref-thatcher_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thatcher-90">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Tourism has become a significant industry, attracting millions of visitors to England each year. The export part of the economy is dominated by <a href="/wiki/Pharmaceuticals" class="mw-redirect" title="Pharmaceuticals">pharmaceuticals</a>, cars (although many English <a href="/wiki/Marque" class="mw-redirect" title="Marque">marques</a> are now foreign-owned, such as <a href="/wiki/Land_Rover" title="Land Rover">Land Rover</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lotus_Cars" title="Lotus Cars">Lotus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jaguar_Cars" title="Jaguar Cars">Jaguar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bentley" title="Bentley">Bentley</a>), <a href="/wiki/Crude_oil" class="mw-redirect" title="Crude oil">crude oil</a> and petroleum from the English parts of <a href="/wiki/North_Sea_oil" title="North Sea oil">North Sea oil</a> along with <a href="/wiki/Wytch_Farm" title="Wytch Farm">Wytch Farm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_engine" title="Aircraft engine">aircraft engines</a> and alcoholic beverages.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Most of the UK\'s \xc2\xa330 billion<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Aerospace_industry_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Aerospace industry in the United Kingdom">aerospace industry</a> is primarily based in England. The global market opportunity for UK aerospace manufacturers over the next two decades is estimated at \xc2\xa33.5 trillion.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/GKN_Aerospace" class="mw-redirect" title="GKN Aerospace">GKN Aerospace</a> \xe2\x80\x93 an expert in metallic and composite aerostructures is involved in almost every civil and military fixed and rotary wing aircraft in production is based in <a href="/wiki/Redditch" title="Redditch">Redditch</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-theengineer.co.uk_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theengineer.co.uk-146">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems" title="BAE Systems">BAE Systems</a> makes large sections of the <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Eurofighter" class="mw-redirect" title="Typhoon Eurofighter">Typhoon Eurofighter</a> at its sub-assembly plant in <a href="/wiki/Salmesbury" class="mw-redirect" title="Salmesbury">Salmesbury</a> and assembles the aircraft for the RAF at its <a href="/wiki/Warton,_Fylde" title="Warton, Fylde">Warton</a> plant, near <a href="/wiki/Preston,_Lancashire" title="Preston, Lancashire">Preston</a>. It is also a principal subcontractor on the <a href="/wiki/F35_Lightning_II" class="mw-redirect" title="F35 Lightning II">F35 Joint Strike Fighter</a> \xe2\x80\x93 the world\'s largest single defence project \xe2\x80\x93 for which it designs and manufactures a range of components including the aft fuselage, vertical and horizontal tail and wing tips and fuel system. It also manufactures the <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems_Hawk" title="BAE Systems Hawk">Hawk</a>, the world\'s most successful jet training aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-theengineer.co.uk_146-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theengineer.co.uk-146">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Rolls-Royce_Holdings" title="Rolls-Royce Holdings">Rolls-Royce PLC</a> is the world\'s second-largest <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_engine" title="Aircraft engine">aero-engine</a> manufacturer. Its engines power more than 30 types of commercial aircraft, and it has more 30,000 engines currently in service across both the civil and defence sectors. With a workforce of over 12,000 people, <a href="/wiki/Derby" title="Derby">Derby</a> has the largest concentration of Rolls-Royce employees in the UK. Rolls-Royce also produces low-emission power systems for ships; makes critical equipment and safety systems for the nuclear industry and powers offshore platforms and major pipelines for the oil and gas industry.<sup id="cite_ref-theengineer.co.uk_146-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theengineer.co.uk-146">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Much of the UK\'s space industry is centred on <a href="/wiki/EADS_Astrium" class="mw-redirect" title="EADS Astrium">EADS Astrium</a>, based in <a href="/wiki/Stevenage" title="Stevenage">Stevenage</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth" title="Portsmouth">Portsmouth</a>. The company builds the <a href="/wiki/Satellite_bus" title="Satellite bus">buses</a> \xe2\x80\x93 the underlying structure onto which the payload and propulsion systems are built \xe2\x80\x93 for most of the <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">European Space Agency</a>\'s spacecraft, as well as commercial <a href="/wiki/Satellites" class="mw-redirect" title="Satellites">satellites</a>. The world leader in compact satellite systems, <a href="/wiki/Surrey_Satellites" class="mw-redirect" title="Surrey Satellites">Surrey Satellites</a>, is also part of Astrium.<sup id="cite_ref-theengineer.co.uk_146-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theengineer.co.uk-146">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Reaction_Engines_Limited" title="Reaction Engines Limited">Reaction Engines Limited</a>, the company planning to build <a href="/wiki/Skylon_(spacecraft)" title="Skylon (spacecraft)">Skylon</a>, a single-stage-to-orbit spaceplane using their <a href="/wiki/SABRE_(rocket_engine)" title="SABRE (rocket engine)">SABRE rocket engine</a>, a combined-cycle, air-breathing rocket propulsion system is based <a href="/wiki/Culham" title="Culham">Culham</a>.\n</p><p>Agriculture is intensive and highly mechanised, producing 60% of food needs with only 2% of the labour force.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> Two-thirds of production is devoted to livestock, the other to arable crops.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_English_inventions_and_discoveries" title="List of English inventions and discoveries">List of English inventions and discoveries</a> and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Society" title="Royal Society">Royal Society</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sir_Isaac_Newton_(1643-1727).jpg" class="image"><img alt="Torso of man with long white hair and dark coloured jacket" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Sir_Isaac_Newton_%281643-1727%29.jpg/170px-Sir_Isaac_Newton_%281643-1727%29.jpg" width="170" height="208" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Sir_Isaac_Newton_%281643-1727%29.jpg/255px-Sir_Isaac_Newton_%281643-1727%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Sir_Isaac_Newton_%281643-1727%29.jpg/340px-Sir_Isaac_Newton_%281643-1727%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="396" data-file-height="484" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sir_Isaac_Newton_(1643-1727).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sir <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Newton" title="Isaac Newton">Isaac Newton</a> is one of the most influential figures in the <a href="/wiki/History_of_science" title="History of science">history of science</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Prominent English figures from the field of science and mathematics include Sir <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Newton" title="Isaac Newton">Isaac Newton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Faraday" title="Michael Faraday">Michael Faraday</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Darwin" title="Charles Darwin">Charles Darwin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Hooke" title="Robert Hooke">Robert Hooke</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Prescott_Joule" title="James Prescott Joule">James Prescott Joule</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Dalton" title="John Dalton">John Dalton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lord_Rayleigh" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Rayleigh">Lord Rayleigh</a>, <a href="/wiki/J._J._Thomson" title="J. J. Thomson">J. J. Thomson</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Chadwick" title="James Chadwick">James Chadwick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Babbage" title="Charles Babbage">Charles Babbage</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Boole" title="George Boole">George Boole</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alan_Turing" title="Alan Turing">Alan Turing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tim_Berners-Lee" title="Tim Berners-Lee">Tim Berners-Lee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Dirac" title="Paul Dirac">Paul Dirac</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Hawking" title="Stephen Hawking">Stephen Hawking</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Higgs" title="Peter Higgs">Peter Higgs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roger_Penrose" title="Roger Penrose">Roger Penrose</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Horton_Conway" title="John Horton Conway">John Horton Conway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Bayes" title="Thomas Bayes">Thomas Bayes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Cayley" title="Arthur Cayley">Arthur Cayley</a>, <a href="/wiki/G._H._Hardy" title="G. H. Hardy">G. H. Hardy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Heaviside" title="Oliver Heaviside">Oliver Heaviside</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Wiles" title="Andrew Wiles">Andrew Wiles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Francis_Crick" title="Francis Crick">Francis Crick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Lister,_1st_Baron_Lister" class="mw-redirect" title="Joseph Lister, 1st Baron Lister">Joseph Lister</a>,  <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Priestley" title="Joseph Priestley">Joseph Priestley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Young_(scientist)" title="Thomas Young (scientist)">Thomas Young</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Wren" title="Christopher Wren">Christopher Wren</a> and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Dawkins" title="Richard Dawkins">Richard Dawkins</a>. Some experts claim that the earliest concept of a <a href="/wiki/Metric_system" title="Metric system">metric system</a> was invented by <a href="/wiki/John_Wilkins" title="John Wilkins">John Wilkins</a>, the first secretary of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Society" title="Royal Society">Royal Society</a>, in 1668.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As the birthplace of the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>, England was home to many significant inventors during the late 18th and early 19th centuries. Famous English engineers include <a href="/wiki/Isambard_Kingdom_Brunel" title="Isambard Kingdom Brunel">Isambard Kingdom Brunel</a>, best known for the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Western_Railway" title="Great Western Railway">Great Western Railway</a>, a series of famous <a href="/wiki/Steamship" title="Steamship">steamships</a>, and numerous important bridges, hence revolutionising public transport and modern-day engineering.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Newcomen" title="Thomas Newcomen">Thomas Newcomen</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Newcomen_steam_engine" class="mw-redirect" title="Newcomen steam engine">steam engine</a> helped spawn the Industrial Revolution.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> The Father of Railways, <a href="/wiki/George_Stephenson" title="George Stephenson">George Stephenson</a>, built the first public inter-city railway line in the world, the <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_and_Manchester_Railway" title="Liverpool and Manchester Railway">Liverpool and Manchester Railway</a>, which opened in 1830. With his role in the marketing and manufacturing of the steam engine, and invention of modern coinage, <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Boulton" title="Matthew Boulton">Matthew Boulton</a> (business partner of <a href="/wiki/James_Watt" title="James Watt">James Watt</a>) is regarded as one of the most influential entrepreneurs in history.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> The physician <a href="/wiki/Edward_Jenner" title="Edward Jenner">Edward Jenner</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Smallpox_vaccine" title="Smallpox vaccine">smallpox vaccine</a> is said to have "saved more lives&#160;... than were lost in all the wars of mankind since the beginning of recorded history."<sup id="cite_ref-saunders_jenner_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-saunders_jenner-154">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-white_jenner_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-white_jenner-155">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-levine_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-levine-156">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Inventions and discoveries of the English include: the <a href="/wiki/Jet_engine" title="Jet engine">jet engine</a>, the first industrial <a href="/wiki/Spinning_frame" title="Spinning frame">spinning machine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Analytical_engine" class="mw-redirect" title="Analytical engine">the first computer</a> and the first <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Baby" title="Manchester Baby">modern computer</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Web" title="World Wide Web">World Wide Web</a> along with <a href="/wiki/HTML" title="HTML">HTML</a>, the first successful human <a href="/wiki/Blood_transfusion" title="Blood transfusion">blood transfusion</a>, the motorised <a href="/wiki/Vacuum_cleaner" title="Vacuum cleaner">vacuum cleaner</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-americanheritage_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-americanheritage-157">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Lawn_mower" title="Lawn mower">lawn mower</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Seat_belt" title="Seat belt">seat belt</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hovercraft" title="Hovercraft">hovercraft</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Electric_motor" title="Electric motor">electric motor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steam_engine" title="Steam engine">steam engines</a>, and theories such as the Darwinian theory of <a href="/wiki/Evolution" title="Evolution">evolution</a> and <a href="/wiki/Atomic_theory" title="Atomic theory">atomic theory</a>. Newton developed the ideas of <a href="/wiki/Universal_gravitation" class="mw-redirect" title="Universal gravitation">universal gravitation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newtonian_mechanics" class="mw-redirect" title="Newtonian mechanics">Newtonian mechanics</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Calculus" title="Calculus">calculus</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Hooke" title="Robert Hooke">Robert Hooke</a> his eponymously named <a href="/wiki/Hooke%27s_law_of_elasticity" class="mw-redirect" title="Hooke&#39;s law of elasticity">law of elasticity</a>. Other inventions include the iron plate railway, the <a href="/wiki/Thermosiphon" title="Thermosiphon">thermosiphon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tarmacadam" title="Tarmacadam">tarmac</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Rubber_band" title="Rubber band">rubber band</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Mousetrap" title="Mousetrap">mousetrap</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cat%27s_eye_(road)" title="Cat&#39;s eye (road)">"cat\'s eye"</a> <a href="/wiki/Raised_pavement_marker" title="Raised pavement marker">road marker</a>, joint development of the <a href="/wiki/Light_bulb" class="mw-redirect" title="Light bulb">light bulb</a>, steam <a href="/wiki/Locomotive" title="Locomotive">locomotives</a>, the modern <a href="/wiki/Seed_drill" title="Seed drill">seed drill</a> and many modern techniques and technologies used in <a href="/wiki/Precision_engineering" title="Precision engineering">precision engineering</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-invent_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-invent-158">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_England" title="Transport in England">Transport in England</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Heathrow_T5.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Planes congregate by a building." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Heathrow_T5.jpg/220px-Heathrow_T5.jpg" width="220" height="107" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Heathrow_T5.jpg/330px-Heathrow_T5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Heathrow_T5.jpg/440px-Heathrow_T5.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1669" data-file-height="815" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Heathrow_T5.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">Heathrow Airport</a> has more international <a href="/wiki/World%27s_busiest_airports_by_international_passenger_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="World&#39;s busiest airports by international passenger traffic">passenger traffic</a> than any other airport in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-airports_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-airports-159">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Department_for_Transport" title="Department for Transport">Department for Transport</a> is the government body responsible for overseeing transport in England. There are many <a href="/wiki/List_of_motorways_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of motorways in the United Kingdom">motorways in England</a>, and many other trunk roads, such as the <a href="/wiki/A1_road_(Great_Britain)" title="A1 road (Great Britain)">A1 Great North Road</a>, which runs through eastern England from London to Newcastle<sup id="cite_ref-roads_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-roads-160">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> (much of this section is motorway) and onward to the Scottish border. The longest motorway in England is the <a href="/wiki/M6_motorway" title="M6 motorway">M6</a>, from <a href="/wiki/Rugby,_Warwickshire" title="Rugby, Warwickshire">Rugby</a> through the <a href="/wiki/North_West_England" title="North West England">North West</a> up to the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Scottish_border" title="Anglo-Scottish border">Anglo-Scottish border</a>, a distance of 232 miles (373&#160;km).<sup id="cite_ref-roads_160-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-roads-160">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> Other major routes include: the <a href="/wiki/M1_motorway" title="M1 motorway">M1</a> from London to Leeds, the <a href="/wiki/M25_motorway" title="M25 motorway">M25</a> which encircles London, the <a href="/wiki/M60_motorway" title="M60 motorway">M60</a> which encircles Manchester, the <a href="/wiki/M4_motorway" title="M4 motorway">M4</a> from London to South Wales, the <a href="/wiki/M62_motorway" title="M62 motorway">M62</a> from Liverpool via Manchester to East Yorkshire, and the <a href="/wiki/M5_motorway" title="M5 motorway">M5</a> from Birmingham to Bristol and the South West.<sup id="cite_ref-roads_160-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-roads-160">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Bus transport across the country is widespread; major companies include <a href="/wiki/National_Express" title="National Express">National Express</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arriva" title="Arriva">Arriva</a> and <a href="/wiki/Go-Ahead_Group" title="Go-Ahead Group">Go-Ahead Group</a>. The red <a href="/wiki/Double-decker_bus" title="Double-decker bus">double-decker buses</a> in London have become a symbol of England. There is a <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">rapid transit</a> network in two English cities: the <a href="/wiki/London_Underground" title="London Underground">London Underground</a>; and the <a href="/wiki/Tyne_and_Wear_Metro" title="Tyne and Wear Metro">Tyne and Wear Metro</a> in Newcastle, Gateshead and Sunderland.<sup id="cite_ref-pubwhite_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pubwhite-161">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> There are several tram networks, such as the <a href="/wiki/Blackpool_tramway" class="mw-redirect" title="Blackpool tramway">Blackpool tramway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Metrolink" title="Manchester Metrolink">Manchester Metrolink</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Supertram" title="Sheffield Supertram">Sheffield Supertram</a> and <a href="/wiki/Midland_Metro" class="mw-redirect" title="Midland Metro">Midland Metro</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Tramlink" title="Tramlink">Tramlink</a> system centred on Croydon in South London.<sup id="cite_ref-pubwhite_161-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pubwhite-161">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Farringdon_station_MMB_22_S-Stock.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Farringdon_station_MMB_22_S-Stock.jpg/220px-Farringdon_station_MMB_22_S-Stock.jpg" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Farringdon_station_MMB_22_S-Stock.jpg/330px-Farringdon_station_MMB_22_S-Stock.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Farringdon_station_MMB_22_S-Stock.jpg/440px-Farringdon_station_MMB_22_S-Stock.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3816" data-file-height="2475" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Farringdon_station_MMB_22_S-Stock.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Railway" title="Metropolitan Railway">Metropolitan Railway</a>, now part of the <a href="/wiki/London_Underground" title="London Underground">London Underground</a> was the first underground railway in the world</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Rail transport in England">Rail transport in England</a> is the oldest in the world: passenger railways originated in England in 1825.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> Much of Britain\'s 10,000 miles (16,000&#160;km) of rail network lies in England, covering the country fairly extensively, although a high proportion of railway lines were closed in the second half of the 20th century. There are plans to reopen lines such as the <a href="/wiki/Varsity_Line" title="Varsity Line">Varsity Line</a> between Oxford and Cambridge. These lines are mostly standard gauge (<a href="/wiki/Single_track_(rail)" class="mw-redirect" title="Single track (rail)">single</a>, <a href="/wiki/Double_track" class="mw-redirect" title="Double track">double</a> or <a href="/wiki/Quadruple_track" title="Quadruple track">quadruple track</a>) though there are also a few <a href="/wiki/British_narrow_gauge_railways" class="mw-redirect" title="British narrow gauge railways">narrow gauge lines</a>. There is rail transport access to France and Belgium through an undersea rail link, the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Tunnel" title="Channel Tunnel">Channel Tunnel</a>, which was completed in 1994.\n</p><p>England has extensive domestic and international aviation links. The largest airport is <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">Heathrow</a>, which is the <a href="/wiki/World%27s_busiest_airports_by_international_passenger_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="World&#39;s busiest airports by international passenger traffic">world\'s busiest airport measured by number of international passengers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-wsj230211_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj230211-163">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> Other large airports include <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport" title="Manchester Airport">Manchester Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stansted_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Stansted Airport">Stansted Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luton_Airport" title="Luton Airport">Luton Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_Airport" title="Birmingham Airport">Birmingham Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-airports_159-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-airports-159">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> By sea there is ferry transport, both local and international, including to Ireland, the Netherlands and Belgium.<sup id="cite_ref-waterworks_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-waterworks-164">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> There are around 4,400 miles (7,100&#160;km) of navigable waterways in England, half of which is owned by the <a href="/wiki/Canal_and_River_Trust" class="mw-redirect" title="Canal and River Trust">Canal and River Trust</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-waterworks_164-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-waterworks-164">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> however, water transport is very limited. The <a href="/wiki/River_Thames" title="River Thames">Thames</a> is the major waterway in England, with imports and exports focused at the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Tilbury" title="Port of Tilbury">Port of Tilbury</a> in the Thames Estuary, one of the United Kingdom\'s three major ports.<sup id="cite_ref-waterworks_164-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-waterworks-164">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Healthcare">Healthcare</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_England" title="Healthcare in England">Healthcare in England</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Queen_Elizabeth_Hospital_Birmingham,_Edgbaston,_Birmingham,_England-7March2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Birds I view of a large hospital." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Queen_Elizabeth_Hospital_Birmingham%2C_Edgbaston%2C_Birmingham%2C_England-7March2011.jpg/220px-Queen_Elizabeth_Hospital_Birmingham%2C_Edgbaston%2C_Birmingham%2C_England-7March2011.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Queen_Elizabeth_Hospital_Birmingham%2C_Edgbaston%2C_Birmingham%2C_England-7March2011.jpg/330px-Queen_Elizabeth_Hospital_Birmingham%2C_Edgbaston%2C_Birmingham%2C_England-7March2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Queen_Elizabeth_Hospital_Birmingham%2C_Edgbaston%2C_Birmingham%2C_England-7March2011.jpg/440px-Queen_Elizabeth_Hospital_Birmingham%2C_Edgbaston%2C_Birmingham%2C_England-7March2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4692" data-file-height="2652" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Queen_Elizabeth_Hospital_Birmingham,_Edgbaston,_Birmingham,_England-7March2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_Hospital_Birmingham" title="Queen Elizabeth Hospital Birmingham">Queen Elizabeth Hospital Birmingham</a>, an NHS hospital, has the largest single floor critical care unit in the world</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Health_Service_(England)" title="National Health Service (England)">National Health Service</a> (NHS) is the <a href="/wiki/Socialised_medicine" class="mw-redirect" title="Socialised medicine">publicly funded healthcare system</a> in England responsible for providing the majority of healthcare in the country. The NHS began on 5 July 1948, putting into effect the provisions of the <a href="/wiki/National_Health_Service_Act_1946" title="National Health Service Act 1946">National Health Service Act 1946</a>. It was based on the findings of the <a href="/wiki/Beveridge_Report" title="Beveridge Report">Beveridge Report</a>, prepared by economist and social reformer <a href="/wiki/William_Beveridge" title="William Beveridge">William Beveridge</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> The NHS is largely funded from general taxation including <a href="/wiki/National_Insurance" title="National Insurance">National Insurance</a> payments,<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> and it provides most of its services free at the point of use, although there are charges for some people for eye tests, dental care, prescriptions and aspects of personal care.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The government department responsible for the NHS is the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Health_(United_Kingdom)" class="mw-redirect" title="Department of Health (United Kingdom)">Department of Health</a>, headed by the <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Health" class="mw-redirect" title="Secretary of State for Health">Secretary of State for Health</a>, who sits in the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Cabinet of the United Kingdom">British Cabinet</a>. Most of the expenditure of the Department of Health is spent on the NHS\xe2\x80\x94\xc2\xa398.6&#160;billion was spent in 2008\xe2\x80\x932009.<sup id="cite_ref-budget2008_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-budget2008-168">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> In recent years the private sector has been increasingly used to provide more NHS services despite opposition by doctors and trade unions.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EWHealthMap.svg" class="image"><img alt="Map of districts in England and Wales shaded by life expectancy." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/EWHealthMap.svg/260px-EWHealthMap.svg.png" width="260" height="265" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/EWHealthMap.svg/390px-EWHealthMap.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/EWHealthMap.svg/520px-EWHealthMap.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="510" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EWHealthMap.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Life expectancy at birth in England and Wales 2012 to 2014. Lighter colours indicate longer life expectancy.</div></div></div>\n<p>The average <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> of people in England is 77.5 years for males and 81.7 years for females, the highest of the four <a href="/wiki/Countries_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Countries of the United Kingdom">countries of the United Kingdom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> The South of England has a higher life expectancy than the North, however, regional differences do seem to be slowly narrowing: between 1991\xe2\x80\x931993 and 2012\xe2\x80\x932014, life expectancy in the North East increased by 6.0 years and in the North West by 5.8 years, the fastest increase in any region outside London, and the gap between life expectancy in the North East and South East is now 2.5 years, down from 2.9 in 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-LifeExpect_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LifeExpect-171">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demography">Demography</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demography_of_England" title="Demography of England">Demography of England</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/English_people" title="English people">English people</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/English_diaspora" title="English diaspora">English diaspora</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cornish_people" title="Cornish people">Cornish people</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_urban_areas_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of urban areas in the United Kingdom">List of urban areas in the United Kingdom</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:England_counties_population_(crop).png" class="image"><img alt="Map of England with regions shaded in different shades of blue." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/England_counties_population_%28crop%29.png/220px-England_counties_population_%28crop%29.png" width="220" height="268" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/England_counties_population_%28crop%29.png/330px-England_counties_population_%28crop%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/England_counties_population_%28crop%29.png/440px-England_counties_population_%28crop%29.png 2x" data-file-width="1083" data-file-height="1321" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:England_counties_population_(crop).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_county" title="Metropolitan county">metropolitan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Non-metropolitan_county" title="Non-metropolitan county">non-metropolitan counties</a>, colour-coded to show population</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:England_and_Wales_population_cartogram_districts.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/England_and_Wales_population_cartogram_districts.svg/220px-England_and_Wales_population_cartogram_districts.svg.png" width="220" height="251" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/England_and_Wales_population_cartogram_districts.svg/330px-England_and_Wales_population_cartogram_districts.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/England_and_Wales_population_cartogram_districts.svg/440px-England_and_Wales_population_cartogram_districts.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1022" data-file-height="1166" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:England_and_Wales_population_cartogram_districts.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Population of England and Wales by administrative areas. Their size is approximately in proportion to their population.  Colours by quints (1/5th) of number of districts classified by population density with division of extreme quints</div></div></div>\n<p>With over 53&#160;million inhabitants, England is by far the most populous country of the United Kingdom, accounting for 84% of the combined total.<sup id="cite_ref-2011census_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011census-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Population_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Population-172">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> England taken as a unit and measured against international states has the fourth largest population in the European Union and would be the 25th largest <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_population_in_2005" title="List of countries by population in 2005">country by population</a> in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> With a density of 424 people per square kilometre, it would be the second most densely populated country in the European Union after <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/English_people" title="English people">English people</a> are a <a href="/wiki/British_people" title="British people">British people</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ethnicityengl_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethnicityengl-176">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> Some genetic evidence suggests that 75\xe2\x80\x9395% descend in the paternal line from prehistoric settlers who originally came from the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a>, as well as a 5% contribution from <a href="/wiki/Angles" title="Angles">Angles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saxons" title="Saxons">Saxons</a>, and a significant Scandinavian (<a href="/wiki/Vikings" title="Vikings">Viking</a>) element.<sup id="cite_ref-opp_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-opp-177">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> However, other geneticists place the <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic</a> estimate up to half.<sup id="cite_ref-UKmaybe_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UKmaybe-180">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> Over time, various cultures have been influential: <a href="/wiki/Prehistoric_Britain" title="Prehistoric Britain">Prehistoric</a>, <a href="/wiki/Britons_(historical)" class="mw-redirect" title="Britons (historical)">Brythonic</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Roman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxon" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-Saxon">Anglo-Saxon</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Viking" class="mw-redirect" title="Viking">Viking</a> (North Germanic),<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gaels" title="Gaels">Gaelic</a> cultures, as well as a large influence from <a href="/wiki/Normans" title="Normans">Normans</a>. There is an English diaspora in former parts of the British Empire; especially the United States, Canada, Australia, South Africa and New Zealand.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;nb 4&#93;</a></sup> Since the late 1990s, many English people <a href="/wiki/British_migration_to_Spain" title="British migration to Spain">have migrated</a> to Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Leave_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leave-191">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:England_ethnicity_estimates_2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Pie chart with main body in blue and multiple smaller segments in other colours." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/England_ethnicity_estimates_2009.jpg/220px-England_ethnicity_estimates_2009.jpg" width="220" height="116" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/England_ethnicity_estimates_2009.jpg/330px-England_ethnicity_estimates_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/England_ethnicity_estimates_2009.jpg/440px-England_ethnicity_estimates_2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1105" data-file-height="581" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:England_ethnicity_estimates_2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>2009 estimates of <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Ethnic groups in the United Kingdom">ethnic groups in England</a><sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>In 1086, when the <i><a href="/wiki/Domesday_Book" title="Domesday Book">Domesday Book</a></i> was compiled, England had a population of two million. About 10% lived in urban areas.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> By 1801, the population was 8.3&#160;million, and by 1901 30.5&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> Due in particular to the economic prosperity of <a href="/wiki/South_East_England" title="South East England">South East England</a>, it has received many economic migrants from the other parts of the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-ethnicityengl_176-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethnicityengl-176">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> There has been <a href="/wiki/Irish_migration_to_Great_Britain" title="Irish migration to Great Britain">significant Irish migration</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> The proportion of ethnically European residents totals at 87.50%, including <a href="/wiki/British_Germans" class="mw-redirect" title="British Germans">Germans</a><sup id="cite_ref-migra_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-migra-196">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Polish_British" class="mw-redirect" title="Polish British">Poles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ethnicityengl_176-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethnicityengl-176">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Other people from much further afield in the former British colonies have arrived since the 1950s: in particular, 6% of people living in England have family origins in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a>, mostly <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ethnicityengl_176-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethnicityengl-176">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-migra_196-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-migra-196">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> 2.90% of the population are black, from Africa and the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>, especially former British colonies.<sup id="cite_ref-ethnicityengl_176-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethnicityengl-176">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-migra_196-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-migra-196">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> There is a significant number of Chinese and <a href="/wiki/British_Chinese" title="British Chinese">British Chinese</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ethnicityengl_176-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethnicityengl-176">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-migra_196-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-migra-196">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> In 2007, 22% of primary school children in England were from <a href="/wiki/Minority_group" title="Minority group">ethnic minority</a> families,<sup id="cite_ref-Paton_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Paton-197">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> and in 2011 that figure was 26.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-Shepherd_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shepherd-198">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> About half of the population increase between 1991 and 2001 was due to immigration.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> Debate over immigration is politically prominent;<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> 80% of respondents in a 2009 <a href="/wiki/Home_Office" title="Home Office">Home Office</a> poll wanted to cap it.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Office_for_National_Statistics" title="Office for National Statistics">ONS</a> has projected that the population will grow by nine million between 2014 and 2039.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>England contains one indigenous national minority, the <a href="/wiki/Cornish_people" title="Cornish people">Cornish people</a>, recognised by the UK government under the <a href="/wiki/Framework_Convention_for_the_Protection_of_National_Minorities" title="Framework Convention for the Protection of National Minorities">Framework Convention for the Protection of National Minorities</a> in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-203">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language">Language</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/English_language_in_England" title="English language in England">English language in England</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English language</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_English_language" class="mw-redirect" title="History of the English language">History of the English language</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish language</a></div>\n<table class="wikitable floatright">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Language\n</th>\n<th>Native speakers<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>English\n</td>\n<td>46,936,780\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish
