data-shorttitle="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="217592" /></audio></div></div>\n<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0"></div></div></td></tr>\n<tr><td colspan="2" class="mbox-text" style="line-height:1.1em"><hr /><span><i>Problems playing these files? See <a href="/wiki/Help:Media" title="Help:Media">media help</a>.</i></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The traditional <a href="/wiki/Folk_music_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Folk music of England">folk music of England</a> is centuries old and has contributed to several genres prominently; mostly <a href="/wiki/Sea_shanties" class="mw-redirect" title="Sea shanties">sea shanties</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jig" title="Jig">jigs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hornpipe" title="Hornpipe">hornpipes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dance_music" title="Dance music">dance music</a>. It has its own distinct variations and regional peculiarities. <a href="/wiki/Wynkyn_de_Worde" title="Wynkyn de Worde">Wynkyn de Worde</a> printed ballads of Robin Hood from the 16th century are an important artefact, as are <a href="/wiki/John_Playford" title="John Playford">John Playford</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dancing_Master" title="The Dancing Master">The Dancing Master</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Harley,_1st_Earl_of_Oxford_and_Earl_Mortimer" title="Robert Harley, 1st Earl of Oxford and Earl Mortimer">Robert Harley\'s</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Roxburghe_Ballads" title="Roxburghe Ballads">Roxburghe Ballads</a></i> collections.<sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup> Some of the best-known songs are <i><a href="/wiki/Greensleeves" title="Greensleeves">Greensleeves</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Pastime_with_Good_Company" title="Pastime with Good Company">Pastime with Good Company</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Maggie_May_(folk_song)" title="Maggie May (folk song)">Maggie May</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Spanish_Ladies" title="Spanish Ladies">Spanish Ladies</a></i> amongst others. Many <a href="/wiki/Nursery_rhymes" class="mw-redirect" title="Nursery rhymes">nursery rhymes</a> are of English origin such as <i><a href="/wiki/Twinkle_Twinkle_Little_Star" class="mw-redirect" title="Twinkle Twinkle Little Star">Twinkle Twinkle Little Star</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Roses_are_red" class="mw-redirect" title="Roses are red">Roses are red</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Jack_and_Jill_(song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Jack and Jill (song)">Jack and Jill</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/London_Bridge_Is_Falling_Down" title="London Bridge Is Falling Down">London Bridge Is Falling Down</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Grand_Old_Duke_of_York" title="The Grand Old Duke of York">The Grand Old Duke of York</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hey_Diddle_Diddle" title="Hey Diddle Diddle">Hey Diddle Diddle</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Humpty_Dumpty" title="Humpty Dumpty">Humpty Dumpty</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup> Traditional English Christmas carols include "<a href="/wiki/We_Wish_You_a_Merry_Christmas" title="We Wish You a Merry Christmas">We Wish You a Merry Christmas</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_First_Noel" title="The First Noel">The First Noel</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/God_Rest_You_Merry,_Gentlemen" title="God Rest You Merry, Gentlemen">God Rest You Merry, Gentlemen</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Fabs.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/The_Fabs.JPG/180px-The_Fabs.JPG" width="180" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/The_Fabs.JPG/270px-The_Fabs.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/The_Fabs.JPG/360px-The_Fabs.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1110" data-file-height="1110" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Fabs.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a> are the most commercially successful and critically acclaimed band in popular music.<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>Early English composers in classical music include Renaissance artists <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Tallis" title="Thomas Tallis">Thomas Tallis</a> and <a href="/wiki/William_Byrd" title="William Byrd">William Byrd</a>, followed up by <a href="/wiki/Henry_Purcell" title="Henry Purcell">Henry Purcell</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Baroque_music" title="Baroque music">Baroque period</a>. German-born <a href="/wiki/George_Frideric_Handel" title="George Frideric Handel">George Frideric Handel</a> became a British subject<sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup> and spent most of his composing life in London, creating some of the most well-known works of classical music, <i><a href="/wiki/Messiah_(Handel)" title="Messiah (Handel)">The Messiah</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Water_Music_(Handel)" class="mw-redirect" title="Water Music (Handel)">Water Music</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Music_for_the_Royal_Fireworks" title="Music for the Royal Fireworks">Music for the Royal Fireworks</a></i>. One of his four <a href="/wiki/Coronation_Anthems_(Handel)" class="mw-redirect" title="Coronation Anthems (Handel)">Coronation Anthems</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Zadok_the_Priest" title="Zadok the Priest">Zadok the Priest</a></i>, composed for the coronation of <a href="/wiki/George_II_of_Great_Britain" title="George II of Great Britain">George II</a>, has been performed at every subsequent <a href="/wiki/Coronation_of_the_British_monarch" title="Coronation of the British monarch">British coronation</a>, traditionally during the sovereign\'s anointing. There was a revival in the profile of composers from England in the 20th century led by <a href="/wiki/Edward_Elgar" title="Edward Elgar">Edward Elgar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Britten" title="Benjamin Britten">Benjamin Britten</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Delius" title="Frederick Delius">Frederick Delius</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gustav_Holst" title="Gustav Holst">Gustav Holst</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Vaughan_Williams" title="Ralph Vaughan Williams">Ralph Vaughan Williams</a> and others.<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup> Present-day composers from England include <a href="/wiki/Michael_Nyman" title="Michael Nyman">Michael Nyman</a>, best known for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Piano" title="The Piano">The Piano</a></i>, and <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Lloyd_Webber" title="Andrew Lloyd Webber">Andrew Lloyd Webber</a>, whose musicals have achieved enormous success in the <a href="/wiki/West_End_theatre" title="West End theatre">West End</a> and worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the field of <a href="/wiki/Popular_music" title="Popular music">popular music</a>, many English bands and solo artists have been cited as the most influential and best-selling musicians of all time. Acts such as <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Led_Zeppelin" title="Led Zeppelin">Led Zeppelin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pink_Floyd" title="Pink Floyd">Pink Floyd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a>, <a href="/wiki/Queen_(band)" title="Queen (band)">Queen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rod_Stewart" title="Rod Stewart">Rod Stewart</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones" title="The Rolling Stones">The Rolling Stones</a> are among the highest selling recording artists in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup> Many musical genres have origins in (or strong associations with) England, such as <a href="/wiki/British_invasion" class="mw-redirect" title="British invasion">British invasion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Progressive_rock" title="Progressive rock">progressive rock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hard_rock" title="Hard rock">hard rock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mod_(subculture)" title="Mod (subculture)">Mod</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glam_rock" title="Glam rock">glam rock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heavy_metal_music" title="Heavy metal music">heavy metal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Britpop" title="Britpop">Britpop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indie_rock" title="Indie rock">indie rock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gothic_rock" title="Gothic rock">gothic rock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shoegazing" title="Shoegazing">shoegazing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Acid_house" title="Acid house">acid house</a>, <a href="/wiki/UK_garage" title="UK garage">garage</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trip_hop" title="Trip hop">trip hop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drum_and_bass" title="Drum and bass">drum and bass</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dubstep" title="Dubstep">dubstep</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Large outdoor <a href="/wiki/List_of_music_festivals_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of music festivals in the United Kingdom">music festivals</a> in the summer and autumn are popular, such as <a href="/wiki/Glastonbury_Festival" title="Glastonbury Festival">Glastonbury</a>, <a href="/wiki/V_Festival" title="V Festival">V Festival</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Reading_and_Leeds_Festivals" title="Reading and Leeds Festivals">Reading and Leeds Festivals</a>. The most prominent <a href="/wiki/Opera_house" title="Opera house">opera house</a> in England is the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Opera_House" title="Royal Opera House">Royal Opera House</a> at <a href="/wiki/Covent_Garden" title="Covent Garden">Covent Garden</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-foreman_301-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foreman-301">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Proms" title="The Proms">The Proms</a> \xe2\x80\x93 a season of <a href="/wiki/Orchestral" class="mw-redirect" title="Orchestral">orchestral</a> classical concerts held primarily at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall" title="Royal Albert Hall">Royal Albert Hall</a> in London \xe2\x80\x93 is a major cultural event in the English calendar, and takes place yearly.<sup id="cite_ref-foreman_301-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foreman-301">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Royal_Ballet" title="The Royal Ballet">The Royal Ballet</a> is one of the world\'s foremost classical ballet companies, its reputation built on two prominent figures of 20th-century dance, <i><a href="/wiki/Prima_ballerina" class="mw-redirect" title="Prima ballerina">prima ballerina</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Margot_Fonteyn" title="Margot Fonteyn">Margot Fonteyn</a> and choreographer <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Ashton" title="Frederick Ashton">Frederick Ashton</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema">Cinema</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Cinema of the United Kingdom">Cinema of the United Kingdom</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ridley_Scott_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Ridley_Scott_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg/190px-Ridley_Scott_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg" width="190" height="253" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Ridley_Scott_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg/285px-Ridley_Scott_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Ridley_Scott_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg/380px-Ridley_Scott_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2306" data-file-height="3074" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ridley_Scott_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ridley_Scott" title="Ridley Scott">Ridley Scott</a> was among a group of English filmmakers, including <a href="/wiki/Tony_Scott" title="Tony Scott">Tony Scott</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alan_Parker" title="Alan Parker">Alan Parker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Hudson" title="Hugh Hudson">Hugh Hudson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adrian_Lyne" title="Adrian Lyne">Adrian Lyne</a>, who emerged from making 1970s UK television commercials.<sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">&#91;293&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>England (and the UK as a whole) has had a considerable influence on the history of the cinema, producing some of the greatest actors, directors and motion pictures of all time, including <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Hitchcock" title="Alfred Hitchcock">Alfred Hitchcock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Chaplin" title="Charlie Chaplin">Charlie Chaplin</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Lean" title="David Lean">David Lean</a>, <a href="/wiki/Laurence_Olivier" title="Laurence Olivier">Laurence Olivier</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vivien_Leigh" title="Vivien Leigh">Vivien Leigh</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Gielgud" title="John Gielgud">John Gielgud</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Sellers" title="Peter Sellers">Peter Sellers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Julie_Andrews" title="Julie Andrews">Julie Andrews</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Caine" title="Michael Caine">Michael Caine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gary_Oldman" title="Gary Oldman">Gary Oldman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Helen_Mirren" title="Helen Mirren">Helen Mirren</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kate_Winslet" title="Kate Winslet">Kate Winslet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Day-Lewis" title="Daniel Day-Lewis">Daniel Day-Lewis</a>. Hitchcock and Lean are among the most critically acclaimed filmmakers.<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup> Hitchcock\'s first thriller, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lodger:_A_Story_of_the_London_Fog" title="The Lodger: A Story of the London Fog">The Lodger: A Story of the London Fog</a></i> (1926), helped shape the <a href="/wiki/Thriller_film" title="Thriller film">thriller</a> genre in film, while his 1929 film, <i><a href="/wiki/Blackmail_(1929_film)" title="Blackmail (1929 film)">Blackmail</a></i>, is often regarded as the first British <a href="/wiki/Sound_film#Transition:_Europe" title="Sound film">sound</a> feature film.<sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">&#91;295&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Major film studios in England include <a href="/wiki/Pinewood_Studios" title="Pinewood Studios">Pinewood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elstree_Studios" title="Elstree Studios">Elstree</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shepperton_Studios" title="Shepperton Studios">Shepperton</a>. Some of the most commercially successful films of all time have been produced in England, including two of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_film_series" class="mw-redirect" title="List of highest-grossing film series">highest-grossing film franchises</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_(film_series)" title="Harry Potter (film series)">Harry Potter</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/James_Bond_(film_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="James Bond (film series)">James Bond</a></i>).<sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ealing_Studios" title="Ealing Studios">Ealing Studios</a> in London has a claim to being the oldest continuously working film studio in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">&#91;297&#93;</a></sup> Famous for recording many motion picture <a href="/wiki/Film_scores" class="mw-redirect" title="Film scores">film scores</a>, the <a href="/wiki/London_Symphony_Orchestra" title="London Symphony Orchestra">London Symphony Orchestra</a> first performed film music in 1935.<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">&#91;298&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/BFI_Top_100_British_films" title="BFI Top 100 British films">BFI Top 100 British films</a> includes <i><a href="/wiki/Monty_Python%27s_Life_of_Brian" title="Monty Python&#39;s Life of Brian">Monty Python\'s Life of Brian</a></i> (1979), a film regularly voted the funniest of all time by the UK public.<sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-308">&#91;299&#93;</a></sup> English producers are also active in <a href="/wiki/International_co-productions" class="mw-redirect" title="International co-productions">international co-productions</a> and English actors, directors and crew feature regularly in American films. The UK film council ranked <a href="/wiki/David_Yates" title="David Yates">David Yates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Nolan" title="Christopher Nolan">Christopher Nolan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Newell_(director)" title="Mike Newell (director)">Mike Newell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ridley_Scott" title="Ridley Scott">Ridley Scott</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paul_Greengrass" title="Paul Greengrass">Paul Greengrass</a> the five most commercially successful English directors since 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-309" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-309">&#91;300&#93;</a></sup> Other contemporary English directors include <a href="/wiki/Sam_Mendes" title="Sam Mendes">Sam Mendes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guy_Ritchie" title="Guy Ritchie">Guy Ritchie</a> and <a href="/wiki/Steve_McQueen_(director)" title="Steve McQueen (director)">Steve McQueen</a>. Current actors include <a href="/wiki/Tom_Hardy" title="Tom Hardy">Tom Hardy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Craig" title="Daniel Craig">Daniel Craig</a>, <a href="/wiki/Benedict_Cumberbatch" title="Benedict Cumberbatch">Benedict Cumberbatch</a> and <a href="/wiki/Emma_Watson" title="Emma Watson">Emma Watson</a>. Acclaimed for his motion capture work, <a href="/wiki/Andy_Serkis" title="Andy Serkis">Andy Serkis</a> opened <a href="/wiki/The_Imaginarium_Studios" class="mw-redirect" title="The Imaginarium Studios">The Imaginarium Studios</a> in London in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-310" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-310">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup> The visual effects company <a href="/wiki/Framestore" title="Framestore">Framestore</a> in London has produced some of the most critically acclaimed special effects in modern film.<sup id="cite_ref-311" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-311">&#91;302&#93;</a></sup> Many successful Hollywood films have been based on English people, <a href="/wiki/British_literature" title="British literature">stories</a> or events. The <a href="/wiki/List_of_Walt_Disney_Animation_Studios_films" title="List of Walt Disney Animation Studios films">\'English Cycle\'</a> of Disney animated films include <i><a href="/wiki/Alice_in_Wonderland" class="mw-redirect" title="Alice in Wonderland">Alice in Wonderland</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Jungle_Book" title="The Jungle Book">The Jungle Book</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Winnie_the_Pooh" class="mw-redirect" title="Winnie the Pooh">Winnie the Pooh</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-312" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-312">&#91;303&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Museums.2C_libraries.2C_and_galleries"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums,_libraries,_and_galleries">Museums, libraries, and galleries</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_museums_in_England" title="List of museums in England">List of museums in England</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:London_Natural_History_Museum_Panorama.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A museum building entrance." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/London_Natural_History_Museum_Panorama.jpg/220px-London_Natural_History_Museum_Panorama.jpg" width="220" height="100" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/London_Natural_History_Museum_Panorama.jpg/330px-London_Natural_History_Museum_Panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/London_Natural_History_Museum_Panorama.jpg/440px-London_Natural_History_Museum_Panorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2500" data-file-height="1140" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:London_Natural_History_Museum_Panorama.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Natural_History_Museum,_London" title="Natural History Museum, London">Natural History Museum</a> in London</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/English_Heritage" title="English Heritage">English Heritage</a> is a governmental body with a broad remit of managing the historic sites, artefacts and environments of England. It is currently sponsored by the <a href="/wiki/Department_for_Culture,_Media_and_Sport" class="mw-redirect" title="Department for Culture, Media and Sport">Department for Culture, Media and Sport</a>. The charity <a href="/wiki/National_Trust_for_Places_of_Historic_Interest_or_Natural_Beauty" title="National Trust for Places of Historic Interest or Natural Beauty">National Trust for Places of Historic Interest or Natural Beauty</a> holds a contrasting role. 17 of the 25 United Kingdom UNESCO <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Sites</a> fall within England.<sup id="cite_ref-313" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313">&#91;304&#93;</a></sup> Some of the best-known of these are: <a href="/wiki/Hadrian%27s_Wall" title="Hadrian&#39;s Wall">Hadrian\'s Wall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stonehenge,_Avebury_and_Associated_Sites" title="Stonehenge, Avebury and Associated Sites">Stonehenge, Avebury and Associated Sites</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tower_of_London" title="Tower of London">Tower of London</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jurassic_Coast" title="Jurassic Coast">Jurassic Coast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saltaire" title="Saltaire">Saltaire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ironbridge_Gorge" title="Ironbridge Gorge">Ironbridge Gorge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Studley_Royal_Park" title="Studley Royal Park">Studley Royal Park</a> and various others.<sup id="cite_ref-314" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-314">&#91;305&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There are many museums in England, but perhaps the most notable is London\'s <a href="/wiki/British_Museum" title="British Museum">British Museum</a>. Its collection of more than seven million objects<sup id="cite_ref-315" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-315">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup> is one of the largest and most comprehensive in the world,<sup id="cite_ref-316" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-316">&#91;307&#93;</a></sup> sourced from every continent, illustrating and documenting the story of human culture from its beginning to the present. The <a href="/wiki/British_Library" title="British Library">British Library</a> in London is the <a href="/wiki/National_library" title="National library">national library</a> and is one of the world\'s largest <a href="/wiki/Research_libraries" class="mw-redirect" title="Research libraries">research libraries</a>, holding over 150&#160;million items in all known languages and formats; including around 25&#160;million books.<sup id="cite_ref-317" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-317">&#91;308&#93;</a></sup> The most senior art gallery is the <a href="/wiki/National_Gallery" title="National Gallery">National Gallery</a> in <a href="/wiki/Trafalgar_Square" title="Trafalgar Square">Trafalgar Square</a>, which houses a collection of over 2,300 paintings dating from the mid-13th century to 1900.<sup id="cite_ref-318" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-318">&#91;309&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Tate" title="Tate">Tate</a> galleries house the national collections of British and international modern art; they also host the famously controversial <a href="/wiki/Turner_Prize" title="Turner Prize">Turner Prize</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-319" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-319">&#91;310&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_England" title="Sport in England">Sport in England</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Queen_presents_the_1966_World_Cup_to_England_Captain,_Bobby_Moore._(7936243534).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/The_Queen_presents_the_1966_World_Cup_to_England_Captain%2C_Bobby_Moore._%287936243534%29.jpg/220px-The_Queen_presents_the_1966_World_Cup_to_England_Captain%2C_Bobby_Moore._%287936243534%29.jpg" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/The_Queen_presents_the_1966_World_Cup_to_England_Captain%2C_Bobby_Moore._%287936243534%29.jpg/330px-The_Queen_presents_the_1966_World_Cup_to_England_Captain%2C_Bobby_Moore._%287936243534%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/The_Queen_presents_the_1966_World_Cup_to_England_Captain%2C_Bobby_Moore._%287936243534%29.jpg/440px-The_Queen_presents_the_1966_World_Cup_to_England_Captain%2C_Bobby_Moore._%287936243534%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1744" data-file-height="1236" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Queen_presents_the_1966_World_Cup_to_England_Captain,_Bobby_Moore._(7936243534).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Queen <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a> presenting the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup_trophy" class="mw-redirect" title="FIFA World Cup trophy">World Cup trophy</a> to 1966 World Cup winning England captain <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Moore" title="Bobby Moore">Bobby Moore</a></div></div></div>\n<p>England has a strong sporting heritage, and during the 19th century codified many sports that are now played around the world. Sports originating in England include association football,<sup id="cite_ref-football_320-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-football-320">&#91;311&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a>, badminton, <a href="/wiki/Squash_(sport)" title="Squash (sport)">squash</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-321" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-321">&#91;312&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rounders" title="Rounders">rounders</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-322" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-322">&#91;313&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hockey" title="Hockey">hockey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Snooker" title="Snooker">snooker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Billiards" class="mw-redirect" title="Billiards">billiards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Darts" title="Darts">darts</a>, table tennis, <a href="/wiki/Bowls" title="Bowls">bowls</a>, <a href="/wiki/Netball" title="Netball">netball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thoroughbred" title="Thoroughbred">thoroughbred</a> horseracing, <a href="/wiki/Greyhound_racing" title="Greyhound racing">greyhound racing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fox_hunting" title="Fox hunting">fox hunting</a>. It has helped the development of <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">golf</a>, sailing and <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a>.\n</p><p>Football is the <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_the_United_Kingdom#Popularity" title="Sport in the United Kingdom">most popular</a> of these sports. The <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England national football team</a>, whose home venue is <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a>, played <a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_football_team" title="Scotland national football team">Scotland</a> in the first ever international football match in 1872.<sup id="cite_ref-323" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-323">&#91;314&#93;</a></sup> Referred to as the "home of football" by <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a>, England hosted the <a href="/wiki/1966_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1966 FIFA World Cup">1966 FIFA World Cup</a>, and won the tournament by defeating <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">West Germany</a> 4\xe2\x80\x932 in the <a href="/wiki/1966_FIFA_World_Cup_Final" title="1966 FIFA World Cup Final">final</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Geoff_Hurst" title="Geoff Hurst">Geoff Hurst</a> scoring a <a href="/wiki/Hat-trick" title="Hat-trick">hat-trick</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-324" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-324">&#91;315&#93;</a></sup> With a British television audience peak of 32.30&#160;million viewers, the final is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_most-watched_television_broadcasts#Most_watched_special_events" title="List of most-watched television broadcasts">most watched television event ever</a> in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-325" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-325">&#91;316&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wembley_Stadium_interior.jpg" class="image"><img alt="The interior of an empty stadium as viewed from its upper tier of seating. The seats are a vivid red and the pitch is a vivid green. The pale grey sky is visible through an opening in the ceiling above the pitch." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Wembley_Stadium_interior.jpg/220px-Wembley_Stadium_interior.jpg" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Wembley_Stadium_interior.jpg/330px-Wembley_Stadium_interior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Wembley_Stadium_interior.jpg/440px-Wembley_Stadium_interior.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2926" data-file-height="1885" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wembley_Stadium_interior.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a>, home of the <a href="/wiki/England_football_team" class="mw-redirect" title="England football team">England football team</a>, has a 90,000 capacity. It is the biggest stadium in the UK</div></div></div>\n<p>At club level, England is recognised by FIFA as the birthplace of club football, due to <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_F.C." title="Sheffield F.C.">Sheffield F.C.</a> founded in 1857 being the world\'s oldest club.<sup id="cite_ref-football_320-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-football-320">&#91;311&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Football_Association" title="The Football Association">The Football Association</a> is the oldest governing body in the sport, with the <a href="/wiki/Laws_of_the_Game_(association_football)" title="Laws of the Game (association football)">rules</a> of football first drafted in 1863 by <a href="/wiki/Ebenezer_Cobb_Morley" title="Ebenezer Cobb Morley">Ebenezer Cobb Morley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-326" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-326">&#91;317&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Football_League" class="mw-redirect" title="The Football League">The Football League</a> were the first cup and league competitions respectively. In the modern day, the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> is the world\'s most-watched football league,<sup id="cite_ref-327" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-327">&#91;318&#93;</a></sup> most lucrative,<sup id="cite_ref-Deloitte2_328-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Deloitte2-328">&#91;319&#93;</a></sup> and amongst the elite.<sup id="cite_ref-329" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-329">&#91;320&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As is the case throughout the UK, football in England is notable for the rivalries between clubs and the passion of the supporters, which includes a tradition of football chants.<sup id="cite_ref-330" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-330">&#91;321&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-331" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-331">&#91;322&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/European_Champion_Clubs%27_Cup" title="European Champion Clubs&#39; Cup">European Cup</a> (now <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a>) has been won by several English clubs.<sup id="cite_ref-332" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-332">&#91;323&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flintoff_bowling_Siddle,_2009_Ashes_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Men in cricket whites play upon a green grass cricket field amidst a stadium." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Flintoff_bowling_Siddle%2C_2009_Ashes_2.jpg/220px-Flintoff_bowling_Siddle%2C_2009_Ashes_2.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Flintoff_bowling_Siddle%2C_2009_Ashes_2.jpg/330px-Flintoff_bowling_Siddle%2C_2009_Ashes_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Flintoff_bowling_Siddle%2C_2009_Ashes_2.jpg/440px-Flintoff_bowling_Siddle%2C_2009_Ashes_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="1152" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flintoff_bowling_Siddle,_2009_Ashes_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/England_cricket_team" title="England cricket team">England</a> playing <a href="/wiki/Australia_national_cricket_team" title="Australia national cricket team">Australia</a> at <a href="/wiki/Lord%27s_Cricket_Ground" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord&#39;s Cricket Ground">Lord\'s Cricket Ground</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2009_Ashes_series" title="2009 Ashes series">2009 Ashes series</a></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">Cricket</a> is generally thought to have been developed in the early medieval period among the farming and metalworking communities of the <a href="/wiki/Weald" title="Weald">Weald</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-333" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-333">&#91;324&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/England_cricket_team" title="England cricket team">England cricket team</a> is a composite England and Wales, team. One of the game\'s top rivalries is <a href="/wiki/The_Ashes" title="The Ashes">The Ashes</a> series between England and <a href="/wiki/Australia_cricket_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Australia cricket team">Australia</a>, contested since 1882. The climax of the <a href="/wiki/2005_Ashes_series" title="2005 Ashes series">2005 Ashes</a> was viewed by 7.4&#160;million as it was available on terrestrial television.<sup id="cite_ref-334" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-334">&#91;325&#93;</a></sup> England has hosted four <a href="/wiki/Cricket_World_Cup" title="Cricket World Cup">Cricket World Cups</a> (1975, 1979, 1983, 1999) and will host the <a href="/wiki/2019_Cricket_World_Cup" title="2019 Cricket World Cup">2019 edition</a>, but never won the tournament, reaching the final 3 times. However they have hosted the <a href="/wiki/ICC_World_Twenty20" title="ICC World Twenty20">ICC World Twenty20</a> in <a href="/wiki/2009_ICC_World_Twenty20" title="2009 ICC World Twenty20">2009</a>, winning this format in 2010 beating rivals Australia in the final. In the domestic competition, the <a href="/wiki/County_Championship" title="County Championship">County Championship</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_County_Cricket_Club" title="Yorkshire County Cricket Club">Yorkshire</a> are by far the most successful club having won the competition 31&#160;times.<sup id="cite_ref-335" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-335">&#91;326&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lord%27s_Cricket_Ground" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord&#39;s Cricket Ground">Lord\'s Cricket Ground</a> situated in London is sometimes referred to as the "Mecca of Cricket".<sup id="cite_ref-336" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-336">&#91;327&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/William_Penny_Brookes" title="William Penny Brookes">William Penny Brookes</a> was prominent in organising the format for the modern <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic Games</a>. In 1994, then President of the <a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">IOC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juan_Antonio_Samaranch" class="mw-redirect" title="Juan Antonio Samaranch">Juan Antonio Samaranch</a>, laid a wreath on Brooke\'s grave, and said, "I came to pay homage and tribute to Dr Brookes, who really was the founder of the modern Olympic Games".<sup id="cite_ref-337" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-337">&#91;328&#93;</a></sup> London has hosted the <a href="/wiki/Summer_Olympic_Games" title="Summer Olympic Games">Summer Olympic Games</a> three times, in <a href="/wiki/1908_Summer_Olympics" title="1908 Summer Olympics">1908</a>, <a href="/wiki/1948_Summer_Olympics" title="1948 Summer Olympics">1948</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">2012</a>. England competes in the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games" title="Commonwealth Games">Commonwealth Games</a>, held every four years. <a href="/wiki/Sport_England" title="Sport England">Sport England</a> is the governing body responsible for distributing funds and providing strategic guidance for sporting activity in England.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:England_world_cup_winners.jpg" class="image"><img alt="White men in grey suits, pale blue shirts and red ties celebrate upon the top floor of an open-top bus. On man holds a golden trophy in the air with one hand." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/England_world_cup_winners.jpg/220px-England_world_cup_winners.jpg" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/England_world_cup_winners.jpg/330px-England_world_cup_winners.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/England_world_cup_winners.jpg/440px-England_world_cup_winners.jpg 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="588" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:England_world_cup_winners.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/England_national_rugby_union_team" title="England national rugby union team">England rugby union team</a> during their victory parade after winning the <a href="/wiki/2003_Rugby_World_Cup" title="2003 Rugby World Cup">2003 Rugby World Cup</a></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">Rugby union</a> originated in <a href="/wiki/Rugby_School" title="Rugby School">Rugby School</a>, Warwickshire in the early 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-338" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-338">&#91;329&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/England_national_rugby_union_team" title="England national rugby union team">England rugby union team</a> won the <a href="/wiki/2003_Rugby_World_Cup" title="2003 Rugby World Cup">2003 Rugby World Cup</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Jonny_Wilkinson" title="Jonny Wilkinson">Jonny Wilkinson</a> scoring the winning <a href="/wiki/Drop_kick" title="Drop kick">drop goal</a> in the last minute of extra time against Australia. England was one of the host nations of the competition in the <a href="/wiki/1991_Rugby_World_Cup" title="1991 Rugby World Cup">1991 Rugby World Cup</a> and also hosted the <a href="/wiki/2015_Rugby_World_Cup" title="2015 Rugby World Cup">2015 Rugby World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-339" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-339">&#91;330&#93;</a></sup> The top level of club participation is the <a href="/wiki/Guinness_Premiership" class="mw-redirect" title="Guinness Premiership">English Premiership</a>. <a href="/wiki/Leicester_Tigers" title="Leicester Tigers">Leicester Tigers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wasps_RFC" title="Wasps RFC">London Wasps</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bath_Rugby" title="Bath Rugby">Bath Rugby</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northampton_Saints" title="Northampton Saints">Northampton Saints</a> have had success in the Europe-wide <a href="/wiki/Heineken_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="Heineken Cup">Heineken Cup</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">Rugby league</a> was born in <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield" title="Huddersfield">Huddersfield</a> in 1895. Since 2008, the <a href="/wiki/England_national_rugby_league_team" title="England national rugby league team">England national rugby league team</a> has been a full test nation in lieu of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_national_rugby_league_team" title="Great Britain national rugby league team">Great Britain national rugby league team</a>, which won three <a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="Rugby League World Cup">World Cups</a> but is now retired. Club sides play in <a href="/wiki/Super_League" title="Super League">Super League</a>, the present-day embodiment of the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Football_League_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Rugby Football League Championship">Rugby Football League Championship</a>. Rugby League is most popular among towns in the northern English counties of <a href="/wiki/Lancashire" title="Lancashire">Lancashire</a>, Yorkshire and <a href="/wiki/Cumbria" title="Cumbria">Cumbria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-340" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-340">&#91;331&#93;</a></sup> All eleven English clubs in Super League are based in the north of England. Some of the most successful clubs include <a href="/wiki/Wigan_Warriors" title="Wigan Warriors">Wigan Warriors</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hull_F.C." title="Hull F.C.">Hull F.C.</a> <a href="/wiki/St_Helens_R.F.C." title="St Helens R.F.C.">St. Helens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Rhinos" title="Leeds Rhinos">Leeds Rhinos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Giants" title="Huddersfield Giants">Huddersfield Giants</a>; the former three have all won the <a href="/wiki/World_Club_Challenge" title="World Club Challenge">World Club Challenge</a> previously.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">Golf</a> has been prominent in England; due in part to its cultural and geographical ties to Scotland, the <a href="/wiki/Golf_in_Scotland" title="Golf in Scotland">home of Golf</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-341" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-341">&#91;332&#93;</a></sup> There are both professional tours for men and women, in two main tours: the <a href="/wiki/Professional_Golfers_Association" title="Professional Golfers Association">PGA</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Tour" class="mw-redirect" title="European Tour">European Tour</a>. England has produced grand slam winners: <a href="/wiki/Cyril_Walker" title="Cyril Walker">Cyril Walker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tony_Jacklin" title="Tony Jacklin">Tony Jacklin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nick_Faldo" title="Nick Faldo">Nick Faldo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Justin_Rose" title="Justin Rose">Justin Rose</a> in the men\'s and <a href="/wiki/Laura_Davies" title="Laura Davies">Laura Davies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alison_Nicholas" title="Alison Nicholas">Alison Nicholas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Karen_Stupples" title="Karen Stupples">Karen Stupples</a> in the women\'s. The world\'s oldest golf tournament, and golf\'s first major is <a href="/wiki/The_Open_Championship" title="The Open Championship">The Open Championship</a>, played both in England and Scotland. The biennial golf competition, the <a href="/wiki/Ryder_Cup" title="Ryder Cup">Ryder Cup</a>, is named after English businessman <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Ryder" title="Samuel Ryder">Samuel Ryder</a> who sponsored the event and donated the trophy.<sup id="cite_ref-342" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-342">&#91;333&#93;</a></sup> Nick Faldo is the most successful Ryder Cup player ever, having won the most points (25) of any player on either the European or US teams.<sup id="cite_ref-343" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-343">&#91;334&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Court_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Court_1.jpg/220px-Court_1.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Court_1.jpg/330px-Court_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Court_1.jpg/440px-Court_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="498" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Court_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Centre_Court" title="Centre Court">Centre Court</a> at <a href="/wiki/The_Championships,_Wimbledon" title="The Championships, Wimbledon">Wimbledon</a>. First played in 1877, the Wimbledon Championships is the oldest tennis tournament in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-344" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-344">&#91;335&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">Tennis</a> was created in Birmingham, England in the late 19th century, and <a href="/wiki/The_Championships,_Wimbledon" title="The Championships, Wimbledon">the Wimbledon Championships</a> is the oldest tennis tournament in the world, and widely considered the most prestigious.<sup id="cite_ref-345" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-345">&#91;336&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-346" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-346">&#91;337&#93;</a></sup> Wimbledon is a tournament that has a major place in the British cultural calendar. <a href="/wiki/Fred_Perry" title="Fred Perry">Fred Perry</a> was the last Englishman to win Wimbledon in 1936. He was the first player to win all four <a href="/wiki/Grand_Slam_in_tennis" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand Slam in tennis">Grand Slam</a> singles titles<sup id="cite_ref-347" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-347">&#91;338&#93;</a></sup> and helped lead the <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_Davis_Cup_team" title="Great Britain Davis Cup team">Great Britain</a> team to four <a href="/wiki/Davis_Cup" title="Davis Cup">Davis Cup</a> wins. English women who have won Wimbledon include: <a href="/wiki/Ann_Haydon_Jones" class="mw-redirect" title="Ann Haydon Jones">Ann Haydon Jones</a> in 1969 and <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Wade" title="Virginia Wade">Virginia Wade</a> in 1977.\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a>, under the <a href="/wiki/Marquess_of_Queensberry_Rules" title="Marquess of Queensberry Rules">Marquess of Queensberry Rules</a>, England has produced many world champions across the weight divisions internationally recognised by the governing bodies. World champions include <a href="/wiki/Bob_Fitzsimmons" title="Bob Fitzsimmons">Bob Fitzsimmons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ted_%22Kid%22_Lewis" title="Ted &quot;Kid&quot; Lewis">Ted "Kid" Lewis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Randolph_Turpin" title="Randolph Turpin">Randolph Turpin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Benn" title="Nigel Benn">Nigel Benn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Eubank" title="Chris Eubank">Chris Eubank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Bruno" title="Frank Bruno">Frank Bruno</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lennox_Lewis" title="Lennox Lewis">Lennox Lewis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ricky_Hatton" title="Ricky Hatton">Ricky Hatton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naseem_Hamed" title="Naseem Hamed">Naseem Hamed</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amir_Khan_(British_boxer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Amir Khan (British boxer)">Amir Khan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carl_Froch" title="Carl Froch">Carl Froch</a>, and <a href="/wiki/David_Haye" title="David Haye">David Haye</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-348" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-348">&#91;339&#93;</a></sup> In women\'s boxing, <a href="/wiki/Nicola_Adams" title="Nicola Adams">Nicola Adams</a> became the world\'s first woman to win an Olympic boxing Gold medal at the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Summer Olympics</a>.\n</p><p>Originating in 17th and 18th-century England, the <a href="/wiki/Thoroughbred" title="Thoroughbred">thoroughbred</a> is a horse breed best known for its use in <a href="/wiki/Horse_racing" title="Horse racing">horse racing</a>. The <a href="/wiki/National_Hunt" class="mw-redirect" title="National Hunt">National Hunt</a> horse race the <a href="/wiki/Grand_National" title="Grand National">Grand National</a>, is held annually at <a href="/wiki/Aintree_Racecourse" title="Aintree Racecourse">Aintree Racecourse</a> in early April. It is the most watched horse race in the UK, attracting casual observers, and three-time winner <a href="/wiki/Red_Rum" title="Red Rum">Red Rum</a> is the most successful racehorse in the event\'s history.<sup id="cite_ref-349" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-349">&#91;340&#93;</a></sup> Red Rum is also the best-known racehorse in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-350" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-350">&#91;341&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mr_Mansell_in_his_Fiat_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1036315.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Mr_Mansell_in_his_Fiat_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1036315.jpg/220px-Mr_Mansell_in_his_Fiat_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1036315.jpg" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Mr_Mansell_in_his_Fiat_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1036315.jpg/330px-Mr_Mansell_in_his_Fiat_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1036315.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Mr_Mansell_in_his_Fiat_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1036315.jpg/440px-Mr_Mansell_in_his_Fiat_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1036315.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="453" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mr_Mansell_in_his_Fiat_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1036315.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Former <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a> world champion <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Mansell" title="Nigel Mansell">Nigel Mansell</a> driving at <a href="/wiki/Silverstone_Circuit" title="Silverstone Circuit">Silverstone</a> in 1990. The circuit hosted the <a href="/wiki/1950_British_Grand_Prix" title="1950 British Grand Prix">first ever Formula One race</a> in 1950</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/1950_British_Grand_Prix" title="1950 British Grand Prix">1950 British Grand Prix</a> at <a href="/wiki/Silverstone_Circuit" title="Silverstone Circuit">Silverstone</a> was the first race in the newly created <a href="/wiki/Formula_One_World_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Formula One World Championship">Formula One World Championship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-351" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-351">&#91;342&#93;</a></sup> Since then, England has produced some of the greatest drivers in the sport, including; <a href="/wiki/John_Surtees" title="John Surtees">John Surtees</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stirling_Moss" title="Stirling Moss">Stirling Moss</a>, <a href="/wiki/Graham_Hill" title="Graham Hill">Graham Hill</a> (only driver to have won the <a href="/wiki/Triple_Crown_of_Motorsport" title="Triple Crown of Motorsport">Triple Crown</a>), <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Mansell" title="Nigel Mansell">Nigel Mansell</a> (only man to hold F1 and IndyCar titles at the same time), <a href="/wiki/Damon_Hill" title="Damon Hill">Damon Hill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Hamilton" title="Lewis Hamilton">Lewis Hamilton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jenson_Button" title="Jenson Button">Jenson Button</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-352" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-352">&#91;343&#93;</a></sup> It has manufactured some of the most technically advanced racing cars, and many of today\'s racing companies choose England as their base of operations for its engineering knowledge and organisation. <a href="/wiki/McLaren_Automotive" title="McLaren Automotive">McLaren Automotive</a>, <a href="/wiki/Williams_F1" class="mw-redirect" title="Williams F1">Williams F1</a>, <a href="/wiki/Team_Lotus" title="Team Lotus">Team Lotus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Honda" title="Honda">Honda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brawn_GP" title="Brawn GP">Brawn GP</a>, <a href="/wiki/Benetton_Formula" title="Benetton Formula">Benetton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Renault" title="Renault">Renault</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Red_Bull_Racing" title="Red Bull Racing">Red Bull Racing</a> are all, or have been, located in the south of England. England also has a rich heritage in <a href="/wiki/Grand_Prix_motorcycle_racing" title="Grand Prix motorcycle racing">Grand Prix motorcycle racing</a>, the premier championship of motorcycle <a href="/wiki/Road_racing" title="Road racing">road racing</a>, and produced several World Champions across all the various class of motorcycle: <a href="/wiki/Mike_Hailwood" title="Mike Hailwood">Mike Hailwood</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Surtees" title="John Surtees">John Surtees</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phil_Read" title="Phil Read">Phil Read</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geoff_Duke" title="Geoff Duke">Geoff Duke</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Barry_Sheene" title="Barry Sheene">Barry Sheene</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mo_Farah_(2)_Moscow_2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Mo_Farah_%282%29_Moscow_2013.jpg/220px-Mo_Farah_%282%29_Moscow_2013.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Mo_Farah_%282%29_Moscow_2013.jpg/330px-Mo_Farah_%282%29_Moscow_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Mo_Farah_%282%29_Moscow_2013.jpg/440px-Mo_Farah_%282%29_Moscow_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="566" data-file-height="378" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mo_Farah_(2)_Moscow_2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mo_Farah" title="Mo Farah">Mo Farah</a> is the most successful British track athlete in modern Olympic Games history, winning the 5000&#160;m and 10,000&#160;m events at two Olympic Games</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Darts" title="Darts">Darts</a> is a widely popular sport in England; a professional competitive sport, darts is a traditional <a href="/wiki/Pub_game" class="mw-redirect" title="Pub game">pub game</a>. The sport is governed by the <a href="/wiki/World_Darts_Federation" title="World Darts Federation">World Darts Federation</a>, one of its member organisations is the <a href="/wiki/British_Darts_Organisation" title="British Darts Organisation">BDO</a>, which annually stages the Lakeside World Professional Championship, the other being the <a href="/wiki/Professional_Darts_Corporation" title="Professional Darts Corporation">Professional Darts Corporation</a> (PDC), which runs its own world championship at <a href="/wiki/Alexandra_Palace" title="Alexandra Palace">Alexandra Palace</a> in London. <a href="/wiki/Phil_Taylor_(darts_player)" title="Phil Taylor (darts player)">Phil Taylor</a> is widely regarded as the best darts player of all time, having won 187 professional tournaments, and a record 16 <a href="/wiki/World_Professional_Darts_Championship" title="World Professional Darts Championship">World Championships</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-353" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-353">&#91;344&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-354" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-354">&#91;345&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Trina_Gulliver" title="Trina Gulliver">Trina Gulliver</a> is the ten-time Women\'s World Professional Darts Champion of the <a href="/wiki/British_Darts_Organisation" title="British Darts Organisation">British Darts Organisation</a>. Another popular sport commonly associated with pub games is <a href="/wiki/Snooker" title="Snooker">Snooker</a>, and England has produced several world champions, including <a href="/wiki/Steve_Davis" title="Steve Davis">Steve Davis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ronnie_O%27Sullivan" title="Ronnie O&#39;Sullivan">Ronnie O\'Sullivan</a>.\n</p><p>The English are keen sailors and enjoy competitive <a href="/wiki/Sailing" title="Sailing">sailing</a>; founding and winning some of the worlds most famous and respected international competitive tournaments across the various race formats, including the <a href="/wiki/Match_race" class="mw-redirect" title="Match race">match race</a>, a regatta, and the <a href="/wiki/America%27s_Cup" title="America&#39;s Cup">America\'s Cup</a>. England has produced some of the world\'s greatest sailors, including, <a href="/wiki/Francis_Chichester" title="Francis Chichester">Francis Chichester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Hasler" title="Herbert Hasler">Herbert Hasler</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Ridgway_(sailor)" title="John Ridgway (sailor)">John Ridgway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robin_Knox-Johnston" title="Robin Knox-Johnston">Robin Knox-Johnston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ellen_MacArthur" title="Ellen MacArthur">Ellen MacArthur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Golding" title="Mike Golding">Mike Golding</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Goodison" title="Paul Goodison">Paul Goodison</a>, and the most successful Olympic sailor ever <a href="/wiki/Ben_Ainslie" title="Ben Ainslie">Ben Ainslie</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-355" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-355">&#91;346&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="National_symbols">National symbols</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/National_symbols_of_England" title="National symbols of England">National symbols of England</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Royal_Arms_of_England.svg" class="image"><img alt="A red shield tapers to its bottom end; on it are three stylised golden lions with blue claws." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Royal_Arms_of_England.svg/170px-Royal_Arms_of_England.svg.png" width="170" height="198" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Royal_Arms_of_England.svg/255px-Royal_Arms_of_England.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Royal_Arms_of_England.svg/340px-Royal_Arms_of_England.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="410" data-file-height="478" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Royal_Arms_of_England.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Arms_of_England" title="Royal Arms of England">Royal Arms of England</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The St George\'s Cross has been the national <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_England" title="Flag of England">flag of England</a> since the 13th century. Originally the flag was used by the maritime <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Genoa" title="Republic of Genoa">Republic of Genoa</a>. The English monarch paid a tribute to the <a href="/wiki/Doge_of_Genoa" title="Doge of Genoa">Doge of Genoa</a> from 1190 onwards so that English ships could fly the flag as a means of protection when entering the Mediterranean.\nA red cross was a symbol for many <a href="/wiki/Crusades" title="Crusades">Crusaders</a> in the 12th and 13th centuries. It became associated with <a href="/wiki/Saint_George" title="Saint George">Saint George</a>, along with countries and cities, which claimed him as their <a href="/wiki/Patron_saint" title="Patron saint">patron saint</a> and used his cross as a banner.<sup id="cite_ref-356" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-356">&#91;347&#93;</a></sup> Since 1606 the St George\'s Cross has formed part of the design of the <a href="/wiki/Union_Flag" class="mw-redirect" title="Union Flag">Union Flag</a>, a Pan-British flag designed by King <a href="/wiki/James_I_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="James I of England">James I</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-flaghistory_229-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flaghistory-229">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tudor_Rose.svg" class="image"><img alt="A red and white flower." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Tudor_Rose.svg/170px-Tudor_Rose.svg.png" width="170" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Tudor_Rose.svg/255px-Tudor_Rose.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Tudor_Rose.svg/340px-Tudor_Rose.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="250" data-file-height="250" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tudor_Rose.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Tudor_rose" title="Tudor rose">Tudor rose</a>, England\'s <a href="/wiki/National_flower" class="mw-redirect" title="National flower">national floral emblem</a></div></div></div>\n<p>There are numerous other symbols and symbolic artefacts, both official and unofficial, including the <a href="/wiki/Tudor_rose" title="Tudor rose">Tudor rose</a>, the nation\'s <a href="/wiki/National_emblem" title="National emblem">floral emblem</a>, and the Three Lions featured on the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Arms_of_England" title="Royal Arms of England">Royal Arms of England</a>. The Tudor rose was adopted as a national emblem of England around the time of the <a href="/wiki/Wars_of_the_Roses" title="Wars of the Roses">Wars of the Roses</a> as a symbol of peace.<sup id="cite_ref-Flowers_357-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flowers-357">&#91;348&#93;</a></sup> It is a <a href="/wiki/Syncreticism" class="mw-redirect" title="Syncreticism">syncretic</a> symbol in that it merged the white rose of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_York" title="House of York">Yorkists</a> and the red rose of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lancaster" title="House of Lancaster">Lancastrians</a>\xe2\x80\x94cadet branches of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Plantagenet" title="House of Plantagenet">Plantagenets</a> who went to war over control of the nation. It is also known as the <i>Rose of England</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Rose_358-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rose-358">&#91;349&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Oak" title="Oak">oak</a> tree is a symbol of England, representing strength and endurance. The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Oak" title="Royal Oak">Royal Oak</a> symbol and <a href="/wiki/Oak_Apple_Day" title="Oak Apple Day">Oak Apple Day</a> commemorate the escape of King <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_England" title="Charles II of England">Charles II</a> from the grasp of the parliamentarians after his father\'s execution: he hid in an oak tree to avoid detection before safely reaching exile.\n</p><p>The Royal Arms of England, a national <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">coat of arms</a> featuring three lions, originated with its adoption by <a href="/wiki/Richard_the_Lionheart" class="mw-redirect" title="Richard the Lionheart">Richard the Lionheart</a> in 1198. It is <a href="/wiki/Blazon" title="Blazon">blazoned</a> as <i>gules, three lions passant guardant or</i> and it provides one of the most prominent symbols of England; it is similar to the traditional arms of <a href="/wiki/Normandy" title="Normandy">Normandy</a>. England does not have an official designated national anthem, as the United Kingdom as a whole has <i><a href="/wiki/God_Save_the_Queen" title="God Save the Queen">God Save the Queen</a></i>. However, the following are often considered unofficial English national anthems:\n<i><a href="/wiki/Jerusalem_(hymn)" class="mw-redirect" title="Jerusalem (hymn)">Jerusalem</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Land_of_Hope_and_Glory" title="Land of Hope and Glory">Land of Hope and Glory</a></i> (used for England during the <a href="/wiki/2002_Commonwealth_Games" title="2002 Commonwealth Games">2002 Commonwealth Games</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-359" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-359">&#91;350&#93;</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/I_Vow_to_Thee,_My_Country" title="I Vow to Thee, My Country">I Vow to Thee, My Country</a></i>. England\'s <a href="/wiki/National_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="National Day">National Day</a> is 23 April which is <a href="/wiki/St_George%27s_Day_in_England" class="mw-redirect" title="St George&#39;s Day in England">St George\'s Day</a>: St George is the patron saint of England.<sup id="cite_ref-St._George_360-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-St._George-360">&#91;351&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span></h2>\n<div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n<ul style="display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold">\n<li style="display:table-row"><span the United Kingdom">Outline of the United Kingdom</a></li></ul></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-12">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">According to the <a href="/wiki/Eurostat" title="Eurostat">European Statistical Agency</a>, London is the largest <a href="/wiki/Larger_Urban_Zone" class="mw-redirect" title="Larger Urban Zone">Larger Urban Zone</a> in the EU, a measure of metropolitan area which comprises a city\'s urban core as well as its surrounding commuting zone. London\'s <a href="/wiki/Largest_cities_of_the_European_Union_by_population_within_city_limits" class="mw-redirect" title="Largest cities of the European Union by population within city limits">municipal population is also the largest in the EU</a>.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-63"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-63">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">As <a href="/wiki/Roger_Scruton" title="Roger Scruton">Roger Scruton</a> explains, "The Reformation must not be confused with the changes introduced into the Church of England during the \'Reformation Parliament\' of 1529\xe2\x80\x9336, which were of a political rather than a religious nature, designed to unite the secular and religious sources of authority within a single sovereign power: the Anglican Church did not make substantial change in doctrine until later."<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-85"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-85">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Figure of 550,000 military deaths is for England and Wales<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-189"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-189">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">For instance, in 1980 around 50&#160;million <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">Americans</a> claimed <a href="/wiki/English_Americans" title="English Americans">English ancestry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> In Canada there are around 6.5&#160;million <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Canada" title="Demographics of Canada">Canadians</a> who claim <a href="/wiki/English_Canadians" title="English Canadians">English ancestry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> Around 70% of <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Australia" class="mw-redirect" title="Demographics of Australia">Australians</a> in 1999 denoted their origins as <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Celtic" title="Anglo-Celtic">Anglo-Celtic</a>, a category which includes all peoples from Great Britain and Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> Chileans of <a href="/wiki/English_Chilean" class="mw-redirect" title="English Chilean">English descent</a> are somewhat of an anomaly in that <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a> itself was never part of the British Empire, but today there are around 420,000 people of English origins living there.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> </span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-pagan-233"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-pagan_233-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-pagan_233-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">People who strictly identified as "Pagan". Other Pagan paths, such as Wicca or Druidism, have not been included in this number.<sup id="cite_ref-2011_ONS_results_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011_ONS_results-232">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-234"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-234">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">People who strictly identified as "Wiccan". Other Pagan paths, such as Druidism, and general "Pagan" have not been included in this number.<sup id="cite_ref-2011_ONS_results_232-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011_ONS_results-232">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-240"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-240">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Students attending English universities now have to pay tuition fees towards the cost of their education, as do English students who choose to attend university in Scotland. Scottish students attending Scottish universities have their fees paid by the devolved Scottish Parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-msnmoney_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-msnmoney-100">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-253"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-253">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">While people such as <a href="/wiki/Norman_Foster_(architect)" class="mw-redirect" title="Norman Foster (architect)">Norman Foster</a> and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Rogers" title="Richard Rogers">Richard Rogers</a> represent the modernist movement, <a href="/wiki/Prince_Charles" class="mw-redirect" title="Prince Charles">Prince Charles</a> since the 1980s has voiced strong views against it in favour of traditional architecture and put his ideas into practice at his <a href="/wiki/Poundbury" title="Poundbury">Poundbury</a> development in Dorset.<sup id="cite_ref-ArchCon4_252-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ArchCon4-252">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> Architects like <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Erith" title="Raymond Erith">Raymond Erith</a>, <a href="/wiki/Francis_Johnson_(architect)" title="Francis Johnson (architect)">Francis Johnson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quinlan_Terry" title="Quinlan Terry">Quinlan Terry</a> continued to practise in the classical style.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-260"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-260">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">These tales may have come to prominence, at least in part, as an attempt by the Norman ruling elite to legitimise their rule of the British Isles, finding <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxon" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-Saxon">Anglo-Saxon</a> history ill-suited to the task during an era when members of the deposed <a href="/wiki/House_of_Wessex" title="House of Wessex">House of Wessex</a>, especially <a href="/wiki/Edgar_the_%C3%86theling" class="mw-redirect" title="Edgar the \xc3\x86theling">Edgar the \xc3\x86theling</a> and his nephews of the Scottish <a href="/wiki/House_of_Dunkeld" title="House of Dunkeld">House of Dunkeld</a>, were still active in the isles.<sup id="cite_ref-higham1_257-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-higham1-257">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> Also <a href="/wiki/Michael_Wood_(historian)" title="Michael Wood (historian)">Michael Wood</a> explains; "Over the centuries the figure of Arthur became a symbol of British history \xe2\x80\x93 a way of explaining the matter of Britain, the relationship between the Saxons and the Celts, and a way of exorcising ghosts and healing the wounds of the past."<sup id="cite_ref-woodbbc_256-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-woodbbc-256">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" Retrieved <span class="nowrap">25 January</span> 2017</span>. <q>The religious settlement that eventually emerged in the reign of Elizabeth gave the Church of England the distinctive identity that it has retained to this day.
